ثلاثاً
The second principle: Sunnah. The establishment of the ruling from Allah, so understand, for it is obligatory to accept. And secondly we [argue] the consensus of the Companions on the obligation of acting upon the report of a trustworthy person. And in this there is no inference from the action of some individuals such that it could be objected that it is not a proof unless it is consensus. And among them is the Commander of the Faithful Ali, and singling him out cuts off what the souls of the Rafidah have whispered—may Allah forsake them—by evidence of what is mutawatir from them. And in it is a reminder to rebut that consensus is ahad, so proving the desired by it would be circular. Acting upon it means acting upon the report of a single narrator, not that their fatwas agreed on the content of the report. And on this basis, it cannot be objected that acting upon another evidence is sufficient, for the utmost is that it agreed with the content of the report. In countless incidents, this yields knowledge that their action was because it was a report of a trustworthy person in a practical matter. And with this it is rebutted that acting upon some reports could be due to accompanying circumstantial evidence and the generality is not established. Without any denial from anyone. And that ordinarily necessitates knowledge due to their agreement, like an explicit statement necessitating knowledge, as in experiential matters. And with this it is rebutted that the consensus is silent consensus, and it does not yield knowledge. Then he detailed some incidents and said: Among that is that all the Companions acted upon the report of the Caliph of the Messenger of Allah, Abu Bakr al-Siddiq, regarding the caliphs being from Quraysh, and 'We prophets do not leave inheritance' and 'Prophets are buried where they die' when they differed about the burial of the Messenger of Allah. This was narrated by Ibn al-Jawzi, as transmitted from al-Taqrir. And the action of that greatest caliph, the greatest Siddiq, Abu Bakr, with the report of al-Mughira regarding the inheritance of the grandmother. Al-Hakim narrated: The grandmother came to Abu Bakr and said: I have a right in the wealth of a son of a son or a son of a daughter who died. He said: I know no right for you in the Book of Allah nor have I heard anything from the Messenger of Allah about it. So he asked, and al-Mughira ibn Shu'bah testified that the Messenger of Allah gave her one-sixth. He said: Is that with you? So Muhammad ibn Salamah testified, and Abu Bakr gave her one-sixth. And al-Hakim narrated from Ubadah ibn al-Samit: Indeed, from the judgment of the Messenger of Allah for the two grandmothers from the inheritance is one-sixth equally between them. And what is famous in the books of usul that his opinion was not to give inheritance to the grandmother until al-Mughira testified is not apparent from the narrated reports on the topic. And the action of the Commander of the Faithful Umar with the report of Abd al-Rahman ibn Awf regarding the jizya of the Magians, who are fire worshippers. Ibn Abi Shaybah narrated that Umar did not take jizya from the Magians until Abd al-Rahman ibn Awf testified that the Messenger of Allah took it from the Magians of Hajar. Thus in al-Durar al-Manthurat and similarly in Sahih al-Bukhari. And the two Imams Malik and al-Shafi'i and Ibn Abi Shaybah narrated from Ja'far from his father that Umar ibn al-Khattab consulted people about the jizya of the Magians, and Abd al-Rahman ibn Awf said: I heard the Messenger of Allah say: Treat them as the People of the Book. And the action of that Faruq with the report of Hamal ibn Malik regarding the imposition of the ghurrah for the fetus. He said: Two women fought, one struck the other and killed her and her fetus, so the Messenger of Allah ruled with a slave or a slave girl and that she be killed for it. This was recorded by the authors of the Sunan, Ibn Hibban, and al-Hakim, as in Sharh Matla' al-Asrar al-Ilahiyyah. And the action of that Faruq with the report of al-Dahhak ibn Sufyan regarding giving inheritance to the wife from the blood money of her husband. Apparent analogy would have rejected it, because blood money is due after the death of the husband, which is the time of termination of marriage. He said: And whoever also heard... That al-Dahhak wrote: The Messenger of Allah gave inheritance to the wife of Ashaym from the blood money of her husband. Recorded by Ahmad and the authors of the Sunan. And the action of that Faruq with the report of Amr ibn Hazm regarding the blood money of fingers. From Sa'id ibn al-Musayyab: Umar judged for the thumb thirteen and for the little finger six, until a writing was found with the family of Amr ibn Hazm that they mentioned was from the Messenger of Allah, and in it: For every finger ten camels. A good hadith recorded by al-Shafi'i and al-Nasa'i, as in the commentary. And the action of the Commander of the Faithful Uthman, the possessor of two lights, and Ali, may Allah be pleased with them, with the report of Fari'ah regarding the 'iddah of death being in the husband's house. Abd al-Razzaq, Abu Dawud, al-Nasa'i, Ibn Majah, and al-Hakim narrated and authenticated it from al-Fari'ah bint Malik ibn Sinan, the sister of Abu Sa'id al-Khudri: She came to the Messenger of Allah asking to return to her family in Banu Khudrah, and that her husband had gone out in pursuit of some slaves of hers who had run away until he caught up with them and they killed him. She said: So I asked the Messenger of Allah to return to my family, for my husband left me no house that he owned nor maintenance. The Messenger of Allah said: Yes. So she left. When she was in the room or in the mosque, he called me (or ordered someone to call me) and said: How did you say? She repeated the story. He said: Stay in your house until the book reaches its term. She said: So I observed 'iddah there for four months and ten days. She said: When Uthman ibn Affan became caliph, he sent for me and asked me about it, so I told him, and he followed it and judged by it. Thus in al-Durar al-Manthurat. Matla' al-Asrar al-Ilahiyyah said: As for the attribution of this story to Ali, God knows best. And the action of Ibn Abbas with the report of Abu Sa'id regarding riba in currency exchange when there is disparity, recanting his former position that there is no riba in currency exchange even if one of the two equivalents is excessive, adducing his statement: 'Riba is in deferment' as in Sahih Muslim, and other examples beyond enumeration. In short, it is well-known among them to adhere to the reports of individuals and act upon them. And the objection that the greatest caliph, the greatest Siddiq, Abu Bakr, objected to al-Mughira ibn Shu'bah until Ibn Salamah narrated as previously, and the Commander of the Faithful Umar objected to the report of Abu Musa al-Ash'ari regarding seeking permission until Abu Sa'id al-Khudri narrated it. Al-Shaykhan, Malik, and Abu Dawud narrated from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri: I was sitting in a gathering of the Ansar when Abu Musa came startled. They said: What frightens you? He said: Umar ordered me to come to him, so I came and asked permission three times but was not granted permission, so I returned. He said: What prevented you from coming to us? I said: I came and greeted at your door but you did not reply, so I returned, and the Messenger of Allah said: If any one of you asks permission three times and is not granted, let him return. He said: You must bring proof for this. They said: Only the youngest of the people would stand. Abu Sa'id stood with him and testified for him. Umar said to Abu Musa: I did not accuse you, but the hadith about the Messenger of Allah... And the Commander of the Faithful Ali objected to the report of Ibn Sinan regarding al-mufawwadah, who is a woman married without a dower or on condition of no dower. Abu Dawud narrated that Ibn Mas'ud said about a man who married a woman and died without consummation and without specifying a dower: She has the full dower and the 'iddah and inheritance. Ma'qil ibn... three times, three times.
Source pages p. 163

Commentary
This passage is a defense of the authority of khabar al-wahid (single-narrator hadith) in Hanafi usul. The author establishes the proof from ijma' al-sahabah (consensus of the Companions). The passage type is a ruling: the Hanafi school asserts that acting upon khabar al-wahid is wajib (obligatory), proven by the fact that the Companions, throughout countless incidents, accepted and acted on such reports without any denier from among them. The author first explains that this consensus is not just the action of some individuals but all Companions, and it includes Ali, which refutes the Rafidah (a Shi'a sect). The consensus is based on their actions, not just fatwas, and it yields certain knowledge like experiential knowledge. Then the author lists numerous examples: Abu Bakr accepting Mughira's report on grandmother's inheritance, Umar accepting reports about jizya for Magians, the ghurrah for fetus, inheritance from blood money, and finger blood money; Uthman and Ali accepting Fari'ah's report on 'iddah; Ibn Abbas recanting his view on riba based on Abu Sa'id's hadith. Finally, the author addresses objections: some Companions initially demanded corroboration (like Abu Bakr with Mughira, Umar with Abu Musa, Ali with Ibn Mas'ud), but these were resolved when additional support came. This shows they did not reject the principle of khabar al-wahid; they only required confirmation in specific cases, and once confirmed, they applied it. Thus, the Hanafi position that khabar al-wahid is a binding proof (hujja) is established.

Key Terms
خبر الواحد (khabar al-wahid): A report transmitted by one or a few narrators that does not reach the level of tawatur.
إجماع الصحابة (ijma' al-sahabah): The consensus of the Companions of the Prophet on a ruling or practice.
حجة (hujja): A proof or evidence that makes a ruling binding.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the primary evidence for the authority of khabar al-wahid?
A) The Quranic verse 'O you who believe, obey Allah and obey the Messenger'
B) The consensus of the Companions on acting upon such reports without denial
C) The rational argument that truth is established by any single narrator
D) The hadith 'May Allah brighten the face of one who hears my words and conveys them'

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school proves that khabar al-wahid is binding by the consensus of the Companions, who consistently acted on such reports without any denier.

Al-Sunnah as Source
intermediate
8 min
Sahaba Practice as Evidence for Khabar al-Wahid
Providing examples of Sahaba acting on khabar al-wahid.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify examples of Sahaba acting on khabar al-wahid and explain how these precedents support the Hanafi position.

Core Idea
The Sahaba consistently acted on solitary reports, proving their authority.

The Hanafi school holds that khabar al-wahid is a binding proof in matters of practice. One of the strongest arguments is the consistent practice of the Sahaba themselves, who accepted and acted upon solitary reports from the Prophet ﷺ. In this lesson, we examine key examples from the source text, including rulings on diyah, 'iddah, and riba, to see how the early community treated ahad reports as authoritative.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi claim
State the Hanafi position: khabar al-wahid is hujjah in 'amal (practice).
This is the core of the disputed issue.
2
Examine the first example: Umar and the diyah of fingers
Analyze how Umar initially ruled based on his own ijtihad but then accepted the hadith of Amr ibn Hazm from the Prophet ﷺ. Note that he changed his ruling upon finding the written report.
This shows that a solitary written report was sufficient to override prior opinion.
3
Analyze the second example: Uthman and Ali with the hadith of Furay'ah
Review how Furay'ah's solitary report about 'iddah was accepted by both Uthman and Ali (though attribution to Ali is uncertain). They acted upon it without requiring multiple narrators.
The report came from a single woman, yet it became the basis for a legal ruling.
4
Consider the third example: Ibn Abbas and riba
Note that Ibn Abbas initially held that riba only applies to credit transactions, but when Abu Sa'id al-Khudri narrated a hadith about riba in currency, Ibn Abbas retracted his earlier view and accepted the solitary report.
This shows that even a single hadith could change the position of a major Sahabi.
5
Synthesize the pattern
The Sahaba did not wait for tawatur; they acted on ahad reports after verifying the narrator's reliability. This consensus in practice (ijma' sukti) demonstrates the binding authority of khabar al-wahid.
The cumulative evidence from multiple incidents strengthens the argument.

That al-Dahhak wrote: The Messenger of Allah ﷺ gave the wife of Ashim inheritance from the blood-money of her husband. Ahmad and the authors of the Sunan narrated it. And the Faruq (Umar) رضي الله عنه acted on the report of Amr ibn Hazm regarding the blood-money of fingers: from Sa'id ibn al-Musayyib that Umar judged for the thumb thirteen (camels) and for the little finger six, until he found a document with the family of Amr ibn Hazm that they mentioned was from the Messenger of Allah ﷺ in which it says: for every finger ten camels – a good hadith narrated by al-Shafi'i and al-Nasa'i, as in the Sharh. And the Commander of the Faithful Uthman the Possessor of the Two Lights and Ali رضي الله تعالى عنهما acted on the report of Furay'ah (with a diminutive fa) that the 'iddah of death is in the husband's house. Abd al-Razzaq, Abu Dawud, al-Nasa'i, Ibn Majah, and al-Hakim (and authenticated it) narrated from Furay'ah bint Malik ibn Sinan, the sister of Abu Sa'id al-Khudri, that she came to the Messenger of Allah ﷺ asking him to return to her family in Banu Khudrah, that her husband had gone out in pursuit of some slaves of hers who had escaped, and when he reached the well-known place he caught up with them and they killed him. She said: I asked the Messenger of Allah ﷺ to return to my family because my husband left me no house he owned nor maintenance, so the Messenger of Allah ﷺ said: 'Yes.' So she left, and when she was in the room or in the mosque, he called me or ordered and I was called, and he said: 'What did you say?' She said: I repeated the story I had mentioned about my husband. He said: 'Stay in your house until the prescribed term reaches its end.' She said: So I observed the 'iddah in it for four months and ten days. She said: When Uthman ibn Affan (became caliph) he sent to me and asked me about it, so I told him, and he followed it and judged by it, as in al-Durar al-Manthurah. The author of Matali' al-Asrar al-Ilahiyyah said: As for attributing this story to the Commander of the Faithful Ali, Allah knows best. And Ibn Abbas acted on the report of Abu Sa'id about riba in currency when there is disparity, retracting from his previous view that there is no riba in currency even if one of the countervalues is excessive, adducing his statement: 'Riba is only in credit transactions' as in Sahih Muslim, and other examples too numerous to recount. In short, it became well-known among them to adhere to ahad reports and to act upon them. (Objection) that the greatest Caliph, al-Siddiq al-Akbar Abu Bakr رضي الله تعالى عنه objected to al-Mughirah ibn Shu'bah until Ibn Salamah narrated it as mentioned earlier, and the Commander of the Faithful Umar رضي الله عنه objected to the report of Abu Musa al-Ash'ari about seeking permission until Abu Sa'id al-Khudri narrated it. The two Shaykhs, Imam Malik, and Abu Dawud narrated from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri that he said: I was sitting in a gathering of the Ansar when Abu Musa came looking alarmed. They said: What frightens you? He said: He (Umar) ordered me to come to him, so I came and sought permission from Umar but he did not permit me, so I returned. He said: What prevented you from coming to us? I said: I came and greeted at your door but you did not respond, so I returned, and the Messenger of Allah ﷺ said: 'When any of you seeks permission three times and is not permitted, let him return.' He said: You must bring me proof of this! They said: Only the youngest of the people will stand. So Abu Sa'id stood with him and testified for him. Umar said to Abu Musa: I do not accuse you, but (I am cautious about) the hadith from the Messenger of Allah ﷺ. And the Commander of the Faithful Ali objected to the report of Ibn Sinan about al-mufawwidah – she who is married without a dower or on condition of no dower. Abu Dawud narrated that Ibn Mas'ud said concerning a man who married a woman and died without consummation and without specifying a dower: she gets the full dower, and on her is the 'iddah, and she receives inheritance. Ma'qil ibn Sinan said: I heard the Messenger of Allah ﷺ judge concerning Barwa' bint Washiq similarly. And he has other narrations. Al-Bayhaqi said: All their chains are authentic, as in Fath al-Qadir. It should not escape you that there is no objection from the Commander of the Faithful Ali here. Rather, it is narrated from his school that she has no dower nor 'iddah, but she inherits. But objection does not necessarily follow, because it is possible that he was not aware of the hadith. And the Mother of the Believers Aishah al-Siddiqah رضي الله عنها objected to the report of Abdullah ibn Umar about the punishment of the deceased due to his family's weeping over him, and the takhrij has been given previously. And the Commander of the Faithful Ali used to swear other than Abu Bakr, according to Fath al-Qadir. The author of Matali' al-Asrar al-Ilahiyyah said: It is not confirmed from him, and among those who denied it is al-Hafiz al-Mundhiri. The summary of the objection is the nullification of consensus by citing disagreement. The answer: They only hesitated when there was doubt about the truthfulness of the narrator or his memory, not because the report is a solitary one. Do you not see that they acted after the joining (of another narrator)? And it is still a solitary report even after joining. And thirdly, we have the tawatur that he (ﷺ) used to send single individuals to convey rulings, among them Mu'adh ibn Jabal, and he never waited for tawatur at all. If ahad were not hujjah, it would not accomplish conveyance; rather it would be misguidance. If you say: If this proof is sound, it would necessitate establishing beliefs by zanni evidence, or that khabar al-wahid yields knowledge. Among those sent was Mu'adh ibn Jabal, and he said to him: 'You are going to a People of the Book, so call them to the testimony that there is no god but Allah' etc. I say: The command regarding the two shahadahs is tawatur for everyone, and they had no doubt that it was commanded by the Messenger of Allah. He only ordered Mu'adh to call to it first because calling the disbelievers to it is an obligation or a sunnah, and because they might believe and thus receive great reward. Understand. It is said: The dispute here is about the obligation of acting (upon the report) for the mujtahid, while those sent to were laymen. That is, it is possible that they were laymen, so (the proof) is not relevant. It may be answered: We grant that those sent to were laymen, but the desired point is there because they were obligated by what the conveyer informed them, because he conveyed to them the words of the infallible Messenger. In this regard, the layman and the mujtahid are equal, for obedience is obligatory upon everyone. The only difference is that the layman does not have the power to understand subtleties, so he relies on the knowledge of another scholar unlike the mujtahid. This does not benefit here. And this is sound speech, but it does not help the disputant, for he may say: Perhaps sending individuals was for them to give fatwa based on their own opinion to laymen, not for narrating reports; that's why jurists were sent, not commoners. I say: It is known by tawatur that in conveying rulings to the mujtahid companions, he (ﷺ) did not require the number of tawatur; rather he sufficed with ahad reports. So those who were sent to were both laymen and also mujtahids. And they were obligated like the general public; if they were not sent to, it would entail delaying conveyance to them. This is very clear. And fourthly, we have the statement of Allah Almighty: {فَلَوْلَا نَفَرَ مِن كُلِّ فِرْقَ مِّنْهُمْ طَائِفَةٌ لِّيَتَفَقَّهُوا فِي الدِّينِ وَلِيُنذِرُوا قَوْمَهُمْ إِذَا رَجَعُوا إِلَيْهِمْ لَعَلَّهُمْ يَحْذَرُونَ} [التوبة: 122]. Meaning: why did not a party from every section go forth to become learned in religion and to warn their people when they return to them so that they may beware? For caution is only concerning what is obligatory. The verse indicates caution, so acting upon the reports of the party is obligatory. And the party from every section does not reach the level of tawatur, rather a party, as Ibn Abbas said, includes one person and a group. And it can be argued that the verse indicates that the going forth of the party for warning by reporting is absolutely determined.
Source pages p. 164

Commentary
This passage is a response to an objection against the binding authority of khabar al-wahid (solitary report). The author first provides examples from the Sahaba acting on ahad reports: Umar acting on the hadith of Amr ibn Hazm regarding finger diyah, Uthman and Ali acting on the report of Furay'ah about 'iddah in the husband's house, and Ibn Abbas retracting his view on riba based on a hadith from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri. Then presents the objection: that some Sahaba (Abu Bakr, Umar, Ali, Aisha) rejected certain ahad reports. The author rebuts that these rejections were due to doubts about the narrator's truthfulness or memory, not because ahad reports are not hujjah. Evidence: the same Sahaba acted on ahad reports after corroboration. Then the author gives two proofs: (1) Tawatur that the Prophet ﷺ sent single individuals (like Mu'adh to Yemen) to teach rulings, proving ahad are hujjah for conveyance. A possible counter-argument that those sent were giving fatwa, not narrating hadith, is addressed by noting that the Prophet ﷺ also conveyed rulings to mujtahid companions via ahad. (2) Quran 9:122 commands a party (طائفة) to warn, and 'party' includes even one person, making it obligatory to accept their warning.

Key Terms
خبر الواحد (khabar al-wahid): A report transmitted by one or a few individuals that does not reach the level of tawatur.
طائفة (ta'ifah): A group or party; according to Ibn Abbas can be one or more.
الإجماع السكوتي (ijma' sukti): Tacit consensus: when some Sahaba act on a ruling and others remain silent, indicating approval.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why did Ibn Abbas change his view on riba in currency?
A) He received a report from a large group of narrators.
B) He heard a hadith from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri, a single narrator.
C) He found a written document from the Prophet ﷺ.
D) He was forced by Uthman.

Key Takeaway
The Sahaba's consistent practice of accepting and acting on khabar al-wahid establishes a strong precedent for its binding authority in Hanafi usul.

Responding to Objections: Why Sahaba Rejected Some Ahad Reports
Refuting objections by examining specific rejections.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to analyze the instances where Sahaba rejected ahad reports and explain the Hanafi rebuttal that these rejections were based on narrator reliability, not a rejection of the principle.

Core Idea
Rejection of a narrator, not the report type, explains Sahaba's initial hesitation.

A common objection against khabar al-wahid is that some Sahaba themselves rejected certain solitary reports. This lesson examines the specific incidents cited by opponents: Abu Bakr with al-Mughirah, Umar with Abu Musa, Ali with Ibn Sinan, and Aisha with Ibn Umar. We then see the Hanafi response: in each case, the objection was not to the category of ahad reports but to the reliability of the individual narrator or the need for confirmation. After verification, they accepted similar reports.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objection
The objection states that prominent Sahaba rejected ahad reports, implying they did not consider them binding.
This is the key counter-evidence.
2
Examine the case of Abu Bakr and al-Mughirah
Abu Bakr asked al-Mughirah for a witness to his report, which was provided by Muhammad ibn Salamah. Once corroborated, Abu Bakr accepted it.
Abu Bakr did not reject the ahad report; he merely wanted confirmation of the narrator's truthfulness.
3
Analyze Umar's case with Abu Musa on isti'dhan
Umar required a witness for Abu Musa's report about seeking permission thrice. Abu Sa'id al-Khudri testified, and Umar accepted the hadith, saying he did not accuse Abu Musa but wanted assurance.
Umar's demand for a witness shows caution about the narrator, not rejection of ahad reports.
4
Consider the case of Ali and Ibn Sinan regarding al-mufawwidah
The passage notes that there is no clear rejection by Ali; rather, his apparent rejection may be due to lack of knowledge of the hadith. He did not reject the principle.
Ali's school held a different view, but that does not constitute rejection of the report's authority.
5
Draw the general Hanafi response
In all cases, the Sahaba only hesitated due to doubts about the narrator's memory or truthfulness, not because they considered ahad reports inherently unreliable. After confirmation, they acted on such reports, which were still ahad.
This distinction protects the principle of khabar al-wahid.

الأخبار ، ولذا بعث الفقهاء لا العوام (أقول : معلوم بالتواتر (أنه عليه وعلى آله وأصحابه الصلاة والسلام في تبليغ الأحكام إلى الصحابة المجتهدين ما كان يفتقر إلى عدد التواتر، بل يكتفي بالآحاد فالمبعوث فِرْقَ مِّنْهُمْ طائفة طايفة إلى قوله : لَعَلَّهُمْ يَحْذَرُونَ ﴾ [التوبة : ۱۲۲] يعني فلولا نفر من كل فرقة منهم ليتفقهوا في الدين ولينذروا قومهم إذا رجعوا إليهم لعلهم يحذرون فإن الحذر إنما يكون من That al-Dahhak wrote: The Messenger of Allah ﷺ gave the wife of Ashim inheritance from the blood-money of her husband. Ahmad and the authors of the Sunan narrated it. And the Faruq (Umar) رضي الله عنه acted on the report of Amr ibn Hazm regarding the blood-money of fingers: from Sa'id ibn al-Musayyib that Umar judged for the thumb thirteen (camels) and for the little finger six, until he found a document with the family of Amr ibn Hazm that they mentioned was from the Messenger of Allah ﷺ in which it says: for every finger ten camels – a good hadith narrated by al-Shafi'i and al-Nasa'i, as in the Sharh. And the Commander of the Faithful Uthman the Possessor of the Two Lights and Ali رضي الله تعالى عنهما acted on the report of Furay'ah (with a diminutive fa) that the 'iddah of death is in the husband's house. Abd al-Razzaq, Abu Dawud, al-Nasa'i, Ibn Majah, and al-Hakim (and authenticated it) narrated from Furay'ah bint Malik ibn Sinan, the sister of Abu Sa'id al-Khudri, that she came to the Messenger of Allah ﷺ asking him to return to her family in Banu Khudrah, that her husband had gone out in pursuit of some slaves of hers who had escaped, and when he reached the well-known place he caught up with them and they killed him. She said: I asked the Messenger of Allah ﷺ to return to my family because my husband left me no house he owned nor maintenance, so the Messenger of Allah ﷺ said: 'Yes.' So she left, and when she was in the room or in the mosque, he called me or ordered and I was called, and he said: 'What did you say?' She said: I repeated the story I had mentioned about my husband. He said: 'Stay in your house until the prescribed term reaches its end.' She said: So I observed the 'iddah in it for four months and ten days. She said: When Uthman ibn Affan (became caliph) he sent to me and asked me about it, so I told him, and he followed it and judged by it, as in al-Durar al-Manthurah. The author of Matali' al-Asrar al-Ilahiyyah said: As for attributing this story to the Commander of the Faithful Ali, Allah knows best. And Ibn Abbas acted on the report of Abu Sa'id about riba in currency when there is disparity, retracting from his previous view that there is no riba in currency even if one of the countervalues is excessive, adducing his statement: 'Riba is only in credit transactions' as in Sahih Muslim, and other examples too numerous to recount. In short, it became well-known among them to adhere to ahad reports and to act upon them. (Objection) that the greatest Caliph, al-Siddiq al-Akbar Abu Bakr رضي الله تعالى عنه objected to al-Mughirah ibn Shu'bah until Ibn Salamah narrated it as mentioned earlier, and the Commander of the Faithful Umar رضي الله عنه objected to the report of Abu Musa al-Ash'ari about seeking permission until Abu Sa'id al-Khudri narrated it. The two Shaykhs, Imam Malik, and Abu Dawud narrated from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri that he said: I was sitting in a gathering of the Ansar when Abu Musa came looking alarmed. They said: What frightens you? He said: He (Umar) ordered me to come to him, so I came and sought permission from Umar but he did not permit me, so I returned. He said: What prevented you from coming to us? I said: I came and greeted at your door but you did not respond, so I returned, and the Messenger of Allah ﷺ said: 'When any of you seeks permission three times and is not permitted, let him return.' He said: You must bring me proof of this! They said: Only the youngest of the people will stand. So Abu Sa'id stood with him and testified for him. Umar said to Abu Musa: I do not accuse you, but (I am cautious about) the hadith from the Messenger of Allah ﷺ. And the Commander of the Faithful Ali objected to the report of Ibn Sinan about al-mufawwidah – she who is married without a dower or on condition of no dower. Abu Dawud narrated that Ibn Mas'ud said concerning a man who married a woman and died without consummation and without specifying a dower: she gets the full dower, and on her is the 'iddah, and she receives inheritance. Ma'qil ibn Sinan said: I heard the Messenger of Allah ﷺ judge concerning Barwa' bint Washiq similarly. And he has other narrations. Al-Bayhaqi said: All their chains are authentic, as in Fath al-Qadir. It should not escape you that there is no objection from the Commander of the Faithful Ali here. Rather, it is narrated from his school that she has no dower nor 'iddah, but she inherits. But objection does not necessarily follow, because it is possible that he was not aware of the hadith. And the Mother of the Believers Aishah al-Siddiqah رضي الله عنها objected to the report of Abdullah ibn Umar about the punishment of the deceased due to his family's weeping over him, and the takhrij has been given previously. And the Commander of the Faithful Ali used to swear other than Abu Bakr, according to Fath al-Qadir. The author of Matali' al-Asrar al-Ilahiyyah said: It is not confirmed from him, and among those who denied it is al-Hafiz al-Mundhiri. The summary of the objection is the nullification of consensus by citing disagreement. The answer: They only hesitated when there was doubt about the truthfulness of the narrator or his memory, not because the report is a solitary one. Do you not see that they acted after the joining (of another narrator)? And it is still a solitary report even after joining. And thirdly, we have the tawatur that he (ﷺ) used to send single individuals to convey rulings, among them Mu'adh ibn Jabal, and he never waited for tawatur at all. If ahad were not hujjah, it would not accomplish conveyance; rather it would be misguidance. If you say: If this proof is sound, it would necessitate establishing beliefs by zanni evidence, or that khabar al-wahid yields knowledge. Among those sent was Mu'adh ibn Jabal, and he said to him: 'You are going to a People of the Book, so call them to the testimony that there is no god but Allah' etc. I say: The command regarding the two shahadahs is tawatur for everyone, and they had no doubt that it was commanded by the Messenger of Allah. He only ordered Mu'adh to call to it first because calling the disbelievers to it is an obligation or a sunnah, and because they might believe and thus receive great reward. Understand. It is said: The dispute here is about the obligation of acting (upon the report) for the mujtahid, while those sent to were laymen. That is, it is possible that they were laymen, so (the proof) is not relevant. It may be answered: We grant that those sent to were laymen, but the desired point is there because they were obligated by what the conveyer informed them, because he conveyed to them the words of the infallible Messenger. In this regard, the layman and the mujtahid are equal, for obedience is obligatory upon everyone. The only difference is that the layman does not have the power to understand subtleties, so he relies on the knowledge of another scholar unlike the mujtahid. This does not benefit here. And this is sound speech, but it does not help the disputant, for he may say: Perhaps sending individuals was for them to give fatwa based on their own opinion to laymen, not for narrating reports; that's why jurists were sent, not commoners. I say: It is known by tawatur that in conveying rulings to the mujtahid companions, he (ﷺ) did not require the number of tawatur; rather he sufficed with ahad reports. So those who were sent to were both laymen and also mujtahids. And they were obligated like the general public; if they were not sent to, it would entail delaying conveyance to them. This is very clear. And fourthly, we have the statement of Allah Almighty: {فَلَوْلَا نَفَرَ مِن كُلِّ فِرْقَ مِّنْهُمْ طَائِفَةٌ لِّيَتَفَقَّهُوا فِي الدِّينِ وَلِيُنذِرُوا قَوْمَهُمْ إِذَا رَجَعُوا إِلَيْهِمْ لَعَلَّهُمْ يَحْذَرُونَ} [التوبة: 122]. Meaning: why did not a party from every section go forth to become learned in religion and to warn their people when they return to them so that they may beware? For caution is only concerning what is obligatory. The verse indicates caution, so acting upon the reports of the party is obligatory. And the party from every section does not reach the level of tawatur, rather a party, as Ibn Abbas said, includes one person and a group. And it can be argued that the verse indicates that the going forth of the party for warning by reporting is absolutely determined.
Source pages p. 164

Commentary
This passage is a response to an objection against the binding authority of khabar al-wahid (solitary report). The author first provides examples from the Sahaba acting on ahad reports: Umar acting on the hadith of Amr ibn Hazm regarding finger diyah, Uthman and Ali acting on the report of Furay'ah about 'iddah in the husband's house, and Ibn Abbas retracting his view on riba based on a hadith from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri. Then presents the objection: that some Sahaba (Abu Bakr, Umar, Ali, Aisha) rejected certain ahad reports. The author rebuts that these rejections were due to doubts about the narrator's truthfulness or memory, not because ahad reports are not hujjah. Evidence: the same Sahaba acted on ahad reports after corroboration. Then the author gives two proofs: (1) Tawatur that the Prophet ﷺ sent single individuals (like Mu'adh to Yemen) to teach rulings, proving ahad are hujjah for conveyance. A possible counter-argument that those sent were giving fatwa, not narrating hadith, is addressed by noting that the Prophet ﷺ also conveyed rulings to mujtahid companions via ahad. (2) Quran 9:122 commands a party (طائفة) to warn, and 'party' includes even one person, making it obligatory to accept their warning.

Key Terms
الانضمام (al-inḍimām): Joining of another narrator; corroboration by a second narrator.
المفوضة (al-mufawwiḍah): A woman married without a dower or on condition of no dower.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi response, why did Umar ask Abu Musa to bring a witness for his hadith?
A) Umar believed that ahad reports require two witnesses.
B) Umar wanted to ensure that the narrator was truthful and the hadith was accurately remembered.
C) Umar rejected all hadith from Abu Musa because he was not a reliable narrator.
D) Umar was testing Abu Musa's memory.

Key Takeaway
Sahaba rejections of ahad reports were due to doubts about specific narrators, not a rejection of the category; after verification, they acted on them.

The Two Main Proofs: Tawatur of Practice and Quran 9:122
Presenting two key proofs and responding to counter-arguments.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi proofs for khabar al-wahid: the tawatur of the Prophet sending single individuals and the Quranic verse 9:122, and respond to potential counter-arguments.

Core Idea
Prophet's consistent sending of single envoys and Quran's command to 'warn' prove solitary reports are binding.

Beyond the practice of the Sahaba, the Hanafi school presents two direct proofs for the authority of khabar al-wahid. First, the tawatur (consecutive transmission) that the Prophet ﷺ used to send single individuals to convey rulings, which would be pointless if ahad reports were not authoritative. Second, the Quranic verse 9:122, which commands a 'party' (ta'ifah) to warn others, and by Hanafi reasoning, ta'ifah can be one person. This lesson analyzes these proofs, addresses counter-arguments, and shows how they establish the binding nature of solitary reports.

Guided Path
1
State the first proof: tawatur of sending individuals
The Prophet ﷺ consistently sent single companions (like Mu'adh to Yemen) to teach rulings. This practice was known to all companions and is itself transmitted tawatur.
If ahad reports were not hujjah, this sending would be futile or misleading.
2
Examine a counter-argument: those sent were giving fatwa, not narrating
The objection says Mu'adh was sent to give his own rulings, not to transmit a hadith. But the text notes that the Prophet ﷺ also conveyed rulings to mujtahid companions via ahad reports, not relying on tawatur.
The response: the Prophet ﷺ did not wait for tawatur even when informing the Sahaba of rulings.
3
State the second proof: Quran 9:122
The verse commands a party (ta'ifah) to become learned and warn their people. The warned must be cautious (yahdharun), which implies acting on the warning.
Linguistic analysis: ta'ifah includes one person, as stated by Ibn Abbas.
4
Analyze the dalalah of the verse
The imperative to warn implies acceptance of the report. 'Cautious' (yahdharun) indicates that the warning must be heeded. Since ta'ifah can be singular, a solitary report triggers obligation.
The dalalah is zanni but sufficient for legal obligation.
5
Synthesize the two proofs
Together, the tawatur of practice and the Quranic verse provide a solid foundation for the Hanafi position, confirming that khabar al-wahid is a binding source of law in practical matters.
These proofs are direct and not dependent on human practice.

ذلك الضحاك كتب رسول الله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم أورث امرأة أشيم من دية زوجها . أخرجه أحمد وأصحاب السنن ( و ) عمل ذلك الفاروق رضي الله عنه (بخبر عمرو بن حزم في دية الأصابع عن سعيد بن المسيب صلى الله عليه وسلم : إذا استأذن أحدكم ثلاثاً فلم يؤذن له فليرجع قال : لتأتيني على هذا بالبينة؟ فقالوا : لا يقوم إلا أصغر القوم، فقام أبو سعيد معه فشهد له، فقال عمر لأبي موسى إني لم أتهمك، ولكن الحديث عنها ولم يدخل ولم يفرض لها فقال لها : الصداق كاملاً وعليها العدة ولها الميراث، فقال معقل بن سنان: سمعت رسول الله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم قضى في بروع بنت واشق بمثله وله روايات أخرى قال البيهقي : كلها أسانيدها صحاح، كذا في فتح القدير». ولا يذهب عليك أنه ليس فيه إنكار أمير المؤمنين علي، نعم قد يروى من مذهبه أنه لا صداق لها ولا عدة ولها الميراث، لكن لا يلزم منه الإنكار لجواز عدم اطلاعه على الحديث و أنكرت أم المؤمنين عائشة الصديقة رضي الله عنها (خبر) عبد الله بن عمر في تعذيب الميت ببكاء أهله عليه وقد تقدم التخريج (وكان أمير المؤمنين علي (يحلف غير أبي بكر ) على ما في «فتح القدير»، قال مطلع الأسرار الإلهية قدس سره: أنه لم يثبت عنه كرم الله وجهه، وممن أنكره الحافظ المنذري، وحاصل الاعتراض إبطال الإجماع بنقل الخلاف والجواب إنما توقفوا عند الريبة) في صدق الراوي أو حفظه لا لأن الخبر من الآحاد ألا ترى أنهم عملوا بعد الانضمام) أي بعد انضمام راو آخر (و) الحال أنه (هو من الآحاد بعد أي بعد الانضمام (و) لنا (ثالثاً تواتر) عنه أنه عليه وآله وأصحابه الصلاة والسلام) يرسل الآحاد لتبليغ الأحكام) ومنهم جبل، ولم يكن ينتظر إلى التواتر قط، فلولا الآحاد حجة لما أفاد التبليغ بل يصير تضليلاً، فإن قلت لو تم هذا الدليل لزم ثبوت العقائد بالدليل الظني أو أفاد خبر الواحد العلم، فإن من المبعوثين معاذ بن جبل، وقد قال له : إنك تأتي قوماً من أهل الكتاب فادعهم إلى شهادة أن لا إله إلا الله الحديث، قلت : الأمر بالشهادتين قد تواتر عند الكل، ولم يكن لهم ريب في أن ذلك مأمور من رسول الله ، وإنما أمر معاذاً بالدعوة إليه أوّلاً، لأن دعوة الكفار إليه أمر أو سنة، ولأنه يحتمل أن يؤمنوا فيثاب ثواباً عظيماً فافهم قيل : النزاع) ههنا (في وجوب عمل المجتهد والمبعوث إليهم كانوا مقلدين) أي يجوز أن يكونوا مقلدين فلا قريب، وقد يجاب عنه سلمنا أن المبعوث إليهم مقلدون لكن فيه المطلوب لأنهم إنما كلفوا بما أخبر المبلغ لأنه بلغهم قول الرسول المعصوم، وفي هذا المقلد والمجتهد سواء فإن الطاعة فرض على كل أحد إنما الفرق بأن المقلد ليس له قوة فهم الدقائق فاكتفى بعلم عالم آخر دون المجتهد، وهذا لا يفيد ههنا وهذا كلام متين إلا أنه لا ينفع المجادل، فإن له أن يقول : لعل إرسال الآحاد للإفتاء برأيهم للمقلدين لا لرواية الأخبار ، ولذا بعث الفقهاء لا العوام (أقول : معلوم بالتواتر (أنه عليه وعلى آله وأصحابه الصلاة والسلام في تبليغ الأحكام إلى الصحابة المجتهدين ما كان يفتقر إلى عدد التواتر، بل يكتفي بالآحاد فالمبعوث إليهم كما كانوا مقلدين كذلك كانوا مجتهدين أيضاً (وهم كانوا مكلفين مثل العامة فلو لم يكونوا مبعوثا إليهم لزم تأخير التبليغ عنهم، وهذا واضح جداً (و) لنا (رابعاً) قوله تعالى: ﴿فَلَوْلَا نَفَرَ مِن كُلِّ فِرْقَ مِّنْهُمْ طائفة طايفة إلى قوله : لَعَلَّهُمْ يَحْذَرُونَ ﴾ [التوبة : ۱۲۲] يعني فلولا نفر من كل فرقة منهم ليتفقهوا في الدين ولينذروا قومهم إذا رجعوا إليهم لعلهم يحذرون فإن الحذر إنما يكون من الواجب والكريمة دلت على الحذر فيكون الأخد بمقتضى أخبار الطائفة واجباً والطائفة من كل فرقة لا تبلغ مبلغ التواتر) بل الطائفة على ما قال ابن عباس رضي الله تعالى عنه تشمل الواحد والجماعة ويمكن أن يقرر أن الكريمة دلت على أن نفور الطائفة للإنذار بالإخبار حتم
That al-Dahhak wrote: The Messenger of Allah ﷺ gave the wife of Ashim inheritance from the blood-money of her husband. Ahmad and the authors of the Sunan narrated it. And the Faruq (Umar) رضي الله عنه acted on the report of Amr ibn Hazm regarding the blood-money of fingers: from Sa'id ibn al-Musayyib that Umar judged for the thumb thirteen (camels) and for the little finger six, until he found a document with the family of Amr ibn Hazm that they mentioned was from the Messenger of Allah ﷺ in which it says: for every finger ten camels – a good hadith narrated by al-Shafi'i and al-Nasa'i, as in the Sharh. And the Commander of the Faithful Uthman the Possessor of the Two Lights and Ali رضي الله تعالى عنهما acted on the report of Furay'ah (with a diminutive fa) that the 'iddah of death is in the husband's house. Abd al-Razzaq, Abu Dawud, al-Nasa'i, Ibn Majah, and al-Hakim (and authenticated it) narrated from Furay'ah bint Malik ibn Sinan, the sister of Abu Sa'id al-Khudri, that she came to the Messenger of Allah ﷺ asking him to return to her family in Banu Khudrah, that her husband had gone out in pursuit of some slaves of hers who had escaped, and when he reached the well-known place he caught up with them and they killed him. She said: I asked the Messenger of Allah ﷺ to return to my family because my husband left me no house he owned nor maintenance, so the Messenger of Allah ﷺ said: 'Yes.' So she left, and when she was in the room or in the mosque, he called me or ordered and I was called, and he said: 'What did you say?' She said: I repeated the story I had mentioned about my husband. He said: 'Stay in your house until the prescribed term reaches its end.' She said: So I observed the 'iddah in it for four months and ten days. She said: When Uthman ibn Affan (became caliph) he sent to me and asked me about it, so I told him, and he followed it and judged by it, as in al-Durar al-Manthurah. The author of Matali' al-Asrar al-Ilahiyyah said: As for attributing this story to the Commander of the Faithful Ali, Allah knows best. And Ibn Abbas acted on the report of Abu Sa'id about riba in currency when there is disparity, retracting from his previous view that there is no riba in currency even if one of the countervalues is excessive, adducing his statement: 'Riba is only in credit transactions' as in Sahih Muslim, and other examples too numerous to recount. In short, it became well-known among them to adhere to ahad reports and to act upon them. (Objection) that the greatest Caliph, al-Siddiq al-Akbar Abu Bakr رضي الله تعالى عنه objected to al-Mughirah ibn Shu'bah until Ibn Salamah narrated it as mentioned earlier, and the Commander of the Faithful Umar رضي الله عنه objected to the report of Abu Musa al-Ash'ari about seeking permission until Abu Sa'id al-Khudri narrated it. The two Shaykhs, Imam Malik, and Abu Dawud narrated from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri that he said: I was sitting in a gathering of the Ansar when Abu Musa came looking alarmed. They said: What frightens you? He said: He (Umar) ordered me to come to him, so I came and sought permission from Umar but he did not permit me, so I returned. He said: What prevented you from coming to us? I said: I came and greeted at your door but you did not respond, so I returned, and the Messenger of Allah ﷺ said: 'When any of you seeks permission three times and is not permitted, let him return.' He said: You must bring me proof of this! They said: Only the youngest of the people will stand. So Abu Sa'id stood with him and testified for him. Umar said to Abu Musa: I do not accuse you, but (I am cautious about) the hadith from the Messenger of Allah ﷺ. And the Commander of the Faithful Ali objected to the report of Ibn Sinan about al-mufawwidah – she who is married without a dower or on condition of no dower. Abu Dawud narrated that Ibn Mas'ud said concerning a man who married a woman and died without consummation and without specifying a dower: she gets the full dower, and on her is the 'iddah, and she receives inheritance. Ma'qil ibn Sinan said: I heard the Messenger of Allah ﷺ judge concerning Barwa' bint Washiq similarly. And he has other narrations. Al-Bayhaqi said: All their chains are authentic, as in Fath al-Qadir. It should not escape you that there is no objection from the Commander of the Faithful Ali here. Rather, it is narrated from his school that she has no dower nor 'iddah, but she inherits. But objection does not necessarily follow, because it is possible that he was not aware of the hadith. And the Mother of the Believers Aishah al-Siddiqah رضي الله عنها objected to the report of Abdullah ibn Umar about the punishment of the deceased due to his family's weeping over him, and the takhrij has been given previously. And the Commander of the Faithful Ali used to swear other than Abu Bakr, according to Fath al-Qadir. The author of Matali' al-Asrar al-Ilahiyyah said: It is not confirmed from him, and among those who denied it is al-Hafiz al-Mundhiri. The summary of the objection is the nullification of consensus by citing disagreement. The answer: They only hesitated when there was doubt about the truthfulness of the narrator or his memory, not because the report is a solitary one. Do you not see that they acted after the joining (of another narrator)? And it is still a solitary report even after joining. And thirdly, we have the tawatur that he (ﷺ) used to send single individuals to convey rulings, among them Mu'adh ibn Jabal, and he never waited for tawatur at all. If ahad were not hujjah, it would not accomplish conveyance; rather it would be misguidance. If you say: If this proof is sound, it would necessitate establishing beliefs by zanni evidence, or that khabar al-wahid yields knowledge. Among those sent was Mu'adh ibn Jabal, and he said to him: 'You are going to a People of the Book, so call them to the testimony that there is no god but Allah' etc. I say: The command regarding the two shahadahs is tawatur for everyone, and they had no doubt that it was commanded by the Messenger of Allah. He only ordered Mu'adh to call to it first because calling the disbelievers to it is an obligation or a sunnah, and because they might believe and thus receive great reward. Understand. It is said: The dispute here is about the obligation of acting (upon the report) for the mujtahid, while those sent to were laymen. That is, it is possible that they were laymen, so (the proof) is not relevant. It may be answered: We grant that those sent to were laymen, but the desired point is there because they were obligated by what the conveyer informed them, because he conveyed to them the words of the infallible Messenger. In this regard, the layman and the mujtahid are equal, for obedience is obligatory upon everyone. The only difference is that the layman does not have the power to understand subtleties, so he relies on the knowledge of another scholar unlike the mujtahid. This does not benefit here. And this is sound speech, but it does not help the disputant, for he may say: Perhaps sending individuals was for them to give fatwa based on their own opinion to laymen, not for narrating reports; that's why jurists were sent, not commoners. I say: It is known by tawatur that in conveying rulings to the mujtahid companions, he (ﷺ) did not require the number of tawatur; rather he sufficed with ahad reports. So those who were sent to were both laymen and also mujtahids. And they were obligated like the general public; if they were not sent to, it would entail delaying conveyance to them. This is very clear. And fourthly, we have the statement of Allah Almighty: {فَلَوْلَا نَفَرَ مِن كُلِّ فِرْقَ مِّنْهُمْ طَائِفَةٌ لِّيَتَفَقَّهُوا فِي الدِّينِ وَلِيُنذِرُوا قَوْمَهُمْ إِذَا رَجَعُوا إِلَيْهِمْ لَعَلَّهُمْ يَحْذَرُونَ} [التوبة: 122]. Meaning: why did not a party from every section go forth to become learned in religion and to warn their people when they return to them so that they may beware? For caution is only concerning what is obligatory. The verse indicates caution, so acting upon the reports of the party is obligatory. And the party from every section does not reach the level of tawatur, rather a party, as Ibn Abbas said, includes one person and a group. And it can be argued that the verse indicates that the going forth of the party for warning by reporting is absolutely determined.
Source pages p. 164

Commentary
This passage is a response to an objection against the binding authority of khabar al-wahid (solitary report). The author first provides examples from the Sahaba acting on ahad reports: Umar acting on the hadith of Amr ibn Hazm regarding finger diyah, Uthman and Ali acting on the report of Furay'ah about 'iddah in the husband's house, and Ibn Abbas retracting his view on riba based on a hadith from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri. Then presents the objection: that some Sahaba (Abu Bakr, Umar, Ali, Aisha) rejected certain ahad reports. The author rebuts that these rejections were due to doubts about the narrator's truthfulness or memory, not because ahad reports are not hujjah. Evidence: the same Sahaba acted on ahad reports after corroboration. Then the author gives two proofs: (1) Tawatur that the Prophet ﷺ sent single individuals (like Mu'adh to Yemen) to teach rulings, proving ahad are hujjah for conveyance. A possible counter-argument that those sent were giving fatwa, not narrating hadith, is addressed by noting that the Prophet ﷺ also conveyed rulings to mujtahid companions via ahad. (2) Quran 9:122 commands a party (طائفة) to warn, and 'party' includes even one person, making it obligatory to accept their warning.

Key Terms
تواتر (tawatur): Consecutive transmission that yields certainty; a report narrated by so many that collusion is impossible.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the significance of Ibn Abbas's interpretation of 'ta'ifah' in Quran 9:122?
A) It proves that ta'ifah always means a group of at least two.
B) It shows that ta'ifah can include a single person, thus supporting khabar al-wahid.
C) It indicates that the verse is about learning, not warning.
D) It was rejected by the other Sahaba.

Key Takeaway
The tawatur of the Prophet sending individuals and Quran 9:122 provide solid evidence for the binding authority of khabar al-wahid in Hanafi usul.

Al-Sunnah as Source
intermediate
10 min
The Prophet's Practice of Sending Solitary Narrators as Proof for Khabar Wahid
Proof of khabar wahid's authority via prophetic practice

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to analyze the Hanafi argument that the Prophet's practice (tawatur) of sending individuals establishes khabar wahid as hujja and evaluate the objections against this proof.

Core Idea
The Prophet's sending of solitary narrators is a mutawatir practice proving khabar wahid is authoritative.

This passage from Fawatih al-Rahmut presents the third proof for the authority of khabar wahid: the prophetic practice (tawatur) of sending individuals to convey rulings. It also addresses objections from those who claim that this practice would imply that beliefs can be based on conjecture. The Hanafi response clarifies the scope of the proof and demonstrates its sufficiency for legal obligations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Dalil
Locate the statement in the passage that describes the Prophet's practice of sending solitary individuals. The text says: 'تواتر عنه أنه كان عليه وآله وأصحابه الصلاة والسلام يرسل الآحاد لتبليغ الأحكام'.
This is the core evidence: a mutawatir practice.
2
Understand the Objection
The opponent argues that if this practice proves khabar wahid is a proof, then it would also imply that beliefs can be established by conjectural evidence (zann). Identify the objection in the passage: 'فإن قلت لو تم هذا الدليل لزم ثبوت العقائد بالدليل الظني'.
The opponent conflates legal rulings with beliefs.
3
Analyze the Hanafi Response
The author responds by distinguishing the scope: Mu'adh was sent with the shahada, which is already mutawatir. The practice is about conveying rulings, not establishing beliefs. Also, the recipients were mujtahids, so they were obliged to act on the solitary report.
The response shows that the proof applies only to legal rulings, not beliefs.
4
Formulate the Final Ruling
Based on this analysis, state the final ruling: khabar wahid is a hujja for legal rulings and must be acted upon, but it does not yield certain knowledge required for beliefs.
This is the conclusion that the Hanafis derive from the prophetic practice.

Source Text

معاذ بن جبل: سمعت رسول الله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم قضى في بروع بنت واشق بمثله وله روايات أخرى قال البيهقي: كلها أسانيدها صحاح، كذا في فتح القدير. ولا يذهب عليك أنه ليس فيه إنكار أمير المؤمنين علي، نعم قد يروى من مذهبه أنه لا صداق لها ولا عدة ولها الميراث، لكن لا يلزم منه الإنكار لجواز عدم اطلاعه على الحديث. وأنكرت أم المؤمنين عائشة الصديقة رضي الله عنها خبر عبد الله بن عمر في تعذيب الميت ببكاء أهله عليه وقد تقدم التخريج. وكان أمير المؤمنين علي يحلف غير أبي بكر على ما في فتح القدير، قال مطلع الأسرار الإلهية قدس سره: أنه لم يثبت عنه كرم الله وجهه، وممن أنكره الحافظ المنذري، وحاصل الاعتراض إبطال الإجماع بنقل الخلاف. والجواب إنما توقفوا عند الريبة في صدق الراوي أو حفظه لا لأن الخبر من الآحاد، ألا ترى أنهم عملوا بعد الانضمام أي بعد انضمام راو آخر، والحال أنه من الآحاد بعد أي بعد الانضمام. ولنا ثالثاً تواتر عنه أنه عليه وآله وأصحابه الصلاة والسلام يرسل الآحاد لتبليغ الأحكام، ومنهم جبل، ولم يكن ينتظر إلى التواتر قط، فلولا الآحاد حجة لما أفاد التبليغ بل يصير تضليلاً. فإن قلت لو تم هذا الدليل لزم ثبوت العقائد بالدليل الظني أو أفاد خبر الواحد العلم، فإن من المبعوثين معاذ بن جبل، وقد قال له: إنك تأتي قوماً من أهل الكتاب فادعهم إلى شهادة أن لا إله إلا الله الحديث، قلت: الأمر بالشهادتين قد تواتر عند الكل، ولم يكن لهم ريب في أن ذلك مأمور من رسول الله، وإنما أمر معاذاً بالدعوة إليه أوّلاً، لأن دعوة الكفار إليه أمر أو سنة، ولأنه يحتمل أن يؤمنوا فيثاب ثواباً عظيماً فافهم. قيل: النزاع ههنا في وجوب عمل المجتهد والمبعوث إليهم كانوا مقلدين أي يجوز أن يكونوا مقلدين فلا قريب، وقد يجاب عنه سلمنا أن المبعوث إليهم مقلدون لكن فيه المطلوب لأنهم إنما كلفوا بما أخبر المبلغ لأنه بلغهم قول الرسول المعصوم، وفي هذا المقلد والمجتهد سواء فإن الطاعة فرض على كل أحد إنما الفرق بأن المقلد ليس له قوة فهم الدقائق فاكتفى بعلم عالم آخر دون المجتهد، وهذا لا يفيد ههنا وهذا كلام متين إلا أنه لا ينفع المجادل، فإن له أن يقول: لعل إرسال الآحاد للإفتاء برأيهم للمقلدين لا لرواية الأخبار، ولذا بعث الفقهاء لا العوام. أقول: معلوم بالتواتر أنه عليه وعلى آله وأصحابه الصلاة والسلام في تبليغ الأحكام إلى الصحابة المجتهدين ما كان يفتقر إلى عدد التواتر، بل يكتفي بالآحاد فالمبعوث إليهم كما كانوا مقلدين كذلك كانوا مجتهدين أيضاً وهم كانوا مكلفين مثل العامة فلو لم يكونوا مبعوثا إليهم لزم تأخير التبليغ عنهم، وهذا واضح جداً.
Mu'adh ibn Jabal narrated: I heard the Messenger of God (peace and blessings be upon him and his family and companions) decree in the case of Barwa' bint Washiq the like of it, and he has other narrations. Al-Bayhaqi said: All its chains are sound, as in Fath al-Qadir. And do not be unaware that there is no denial from the Commander of the Faithful 'Ali in it. Rather, it may be narrated from his school that she has no dower and no waiting period and she has inheritance, but denial does not necessarily follow because of the possibility of his not being aware of the hadith. And the Mother of the Believers 'Aisha al-Siddiqa (may God be pleased with her) denied the report of 'Abdullah ibn 'Umar about the punishment of the deceased by the weeping of his family, and the takhrij has preceded. And the Commander of the Faithful 'Ali used to swear other than Abu Bakr, according to what is in Fath al-Qadir. The author of Muttali' al-Asrar, may his secret be sanctified, said: It is not established from him (may God honor his face), and among those who denied it is al-Hafiz al-Mundhiri. The summary of the objection is to invalidate consensus by reporting disagreement. The answer: They only hesitated due to doubt about the truthfulness of the narrator or his memory, not because the report is from the solitary category. Do you not see that they acted after joining, i.e., after the addition of another narrator, while it is still from the solitary after joining? And thirdly, we have tawatur from him (peace and blessings be upon him and his family and companions) that he used to send solitary individuals to convey rulings, among them Jabal, and he never waited for tawatur at all. If solitary reports were not proof, they would not have been effective for conveying, rather it would be misguidance. If you say: If this proof holds, it would lead to establishing beliefs by conjectural evidence, or that a solitary report would give knowledge. Indeed, among those sent was Mu'adh ibn Jabal, and he said to him: 'You are going to a people from the People of the Book, so call them to the testimony that there is no god but God,' the hadith. I say: The command to the two testimonies is mutawatir among all, and they had no doubt that it was commanded by the Messenger of God. He only ordered Mu'adh to call to it first, because calling the disbelievers to it is a command or a sunna, and because it is possible that they might believe and he would receive a great reward. So understand. It was said: The dispute here is about the obligation of acting of the mujtahid, and those sent to were muqallids, i.e., it is possible they were muqallids, so it is not near. And it may be answered: We grant that those sent to were muqallids, but the objective is achieved because they are obliged by what the conveyer reported because he conveyed the words of the infallible Messenger. In this, the muqallid and the mujtahid are equal, for obedience is obligatory upon everyone. The difference is only that the muqallid does not have the strength to understand subtleties, so he suffices with the knowledge of another scholar without the mujtahid. This does not benefit here. This is solid speech, but it does not help the disputer, for he may say: Perhaps sending solitary individuals was for issuing legal opinions by their opinion to the muqallids, not for narrating reports. Hence, he sent jurists, not laymen. I say: It is known by tawatur that he (peace and blessings be upon him and his family and companions) in conveying rulings to the mujtahid companions did not need a tawatur number, but sufficed with solitary reports. So those sent to, as they were muqallids, were also mujtahids, and they were obliged like the general public. If they were not sent to, it would lead to delay in conveying to them. This is very clear.
Source pages p. 165

Commentary
This passage is an expansion of the proof for the authority of khabar wahid. It begins by addressing the objection that some Companions denied certain ahadith. The author clarifies that such denials were due to doubt about the narrator's reliability or memory, not a rejection of khabar wahid in principle. The second part presents the third proof: the practice (tawatur) of the Prophet sending solitary individuals to convey rulings. This establishes that khabar wahid is hujja. The author then addresses the objection that using this proof would imply that beliefs could be based on conjecture. The response is that the Prophet sent Mu'adh with a message that was already mutawatir (the shahada), so the proof is about legal rulings, not beliefs. Next, the objection that the recipients might be muqallids is considered. The author concedes the possibility but argues that the objective is still achieved because even muqallids are obligated to follow the conveyed report. However, a stronger response is that the Prophet sent to mujtahids as well, who needed no other authority. The conclusion is clear: the Prophet's practice demonstrates that khabar wahid is sufficient for conveying rulings.

Key Terms
الآحاد (al-āhād): Solitary reports (khabar wahid) that do not meet the conditions of tawatur.
تواتر (tawātur): A report transmitted by a large number of narrators in each generation, precluding collusion, yielding certain knowledge.
حجة (ḥujja): A proof or evidence that is authoritative and must be acted upon.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Consensus of the Companions
B) The Prophet's practice of sending solitary individuals to convey rulings
C) The Quranic verse in Surah al-Tawbah
D) The analogy with qiyas

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's mutawatir practice of sending solitary narrators proves that khabar wahid is a valid proof (hujja) for legal rulings, and the Hanafi response to objections clarifies its scope.

Establishing the Obligation of Khabar al-Wahid: Quranic Evidence and the Mafhum Debate
Establishing obligation through Quran and consensus, with mafhum analysis

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to analyze the Hanafi derivation of the obligation to act on khabar al-wahid from Quran 49:6, and evaluate the role of mafhum al-sifah versus mafhum al-shart in that derivation.

Core Idea
The obligation to accept khabar al-wahid is founded on consensus; the Quranic verse 49:6 provides supporting evidence through mafhum al-sifah, not mafhum al-shart.

This passage tackles a foundational question in Hanafi usul: how do we know that a khabar al-wahid (single-narrator report) must be acted upon? While the ultimate basis is consensus (ijma'), the author also engages with the Quranic verse 'If a sinful person brings you news, investigate...' (49:6). But the deduction from this verse is not straightforward—it requires careful analysis of the type of mafhum (implication) at work. The text also refutes rational arguments and addresses objections about incidents being devoid of rulings. By working through this passage, you will learn how Hanafi usul uses mafhum al-sifah to derive a ruling and how it defends against objections.

Guided Path
1
Identify the primary basis for obligation
The passage begins by stating that knowledge of the obligation comes from consensus (ijma') on acting on zann from the Quran's apparent meaning. This is the central foundation—not the verse alone.
The verse is supporting evidence, not the root proof.
2
Locate the Quranic proof
The verse 49:6 is cited. Note the command to investigate when a fasiq brings news. What does this imply about a just reporter?
3
Distinguish between mafhum al-shart and mafhum al-sifah
The author explains that the correct deduction is through mafhum al-sifah (the attribute 'fasiq' implies the opposite for a just person), not mafhum al-shart (if not fasiq, then no investigation). Why is mafhum al-sifah preferred? Because it gives a specific and useful ruling, whereas mafhum al-shart would lead to a trivial conclusion.
This distinction is crucial for the Hanafi rebuttal.
4
Address objections
The text considers the objection that mafhum is weak and that the verse alone cannot prove the obligation. The answer: consensus is added to strengthen the evidence.
5
Evaluate rational arguments
The passage critiques rational claims for obligation, showing that the real basis is legal (shar'i), not purely rational. It also counters the argument that most incidents would be devoid of rulings.

بوجوب التعبد به بالعقل) فمنهم من قال : وجوب الاجتناب عن المضار معلوم عقلاً، وهذا أصل كلي يعتقده الخاصة والعامة والعمل بالظن في تفاصيل مقطوع الأصل واجب عقلاً، كأخبار واحد بمضرة طعام وسقوط حائط) فإنه الصوم بالشك) في رؤية هلال رمضان الشريف، ولا يذهب عليك أنه ما ادعى وجوب الاحتياط مطلقاً، بل الاحتياط في المظنون ولا شك فيه وأما عدم وجوب صوم يوم الشك فلعدم الظن هناك، فالأحرى منع كون الاحتياط واجباً عقلاً بل إنما يجب فيما يجب سمعاً (و) استدل (ثانياً: لو لم يجب العمل بخبر الواحد (الخلت الوقائع أكثرها ( عن الأحكام ، لأن القرآن والمتواتر) من السنة (لا يفيان بجميع الوقائع بل ما يفيان به أقل القليل والجواب منع الملازمة، لأن حكم عند عدم الدليل عدم الحكم بالشرع وهذا يشتمل جميع الوقائع الخالية عن القطع إذ هو الدليل فيتوقف أو يعمل بالإباحة الأصلية على اختلاف القولين، كما قد مر ، والأظهر الإباحة فيما Knowledge of the obligation to act on a single-narrator report is necessary, because there is consensus on the obligation to act on the probability obtained from the apparent meaning of the Book, nothing else. Understand, for it is subtle, as if recognized yet denied. And he adduced evidence by His statement: 'If a sinful person brings you news, investigate...' (49:6). For it indicates that if a just person comes to you, accept his statement. And this deduction is based on the concept of contrary implication (mafhum al-mukhalafah), so the Hanafi who denies it cannot use it as evidence. Also, even if conceded, it is a weak probable indication, not suitable as proof in matters requiring certainty. But you can refute by what preceded: adding consensus to it. It was also objected that the concept of the condition is: if no sinful person brings news, do not investigate, which is more general than accepting the report of a just person or no report at all. The answer: the concept is established so that benefit is not lost, but here there is no benefit at all, as it is known beforehand. The truth is that the deduction is not by the concept of the condition, but by the concept of the attribute, for 'sinful' is an attribute, and its concept is: if a non-sinful person comes, i.e., the just, then accept. Understand. (As for those who cling to the obligation of devotion to it by reason), some of them said: The obligation to avoid harms is known by reason, and this is a universal principle believed by elite and commoners alike. Acting upon probability in details concerning a certain origin is rationally obligatory, like a report of a single person about harm of food or a falling wall, for it is obligatory to accept. And the statement of the Messenger explains harms and benefits, so if one is probable about it, action is definitely obligatory. This is based on reason's judgment of obligation, which has passed before, so it does not stand as proof against those who do not accept it. Moreover, the obligation to act upon probability in such details is denied; rather, this action is rationally preferable. Yes, the obligation of this matter is established by law. (Some of them adduced first that his truthfulness is probable, necessarily, so action is obligatory as a precaution). It is objected that precaution is not obligatory absolutely; do you not see that fasting is not obligatory on the doubt of sighting the crescent of Ramadan? And it should not escape you that he did not claim absolute obligation of precaution, but precaution in probable matters, and there is no doubt about that. As for the non-obligation of fasting on the day of doubt, it is because there is no probability there. So it is more fitting to deny that precaution is rationally obligatory; rather, it is only obligatory in what is heard. (And they adduced secondarily: If acting on a single report were not obligatory, most incidents would be devoid of rulings, because the Quran and mutawatir Sunnah do not cover all incidents; what they cover is minimal. The answer: deny the entailment, because the ruling in the absence of evidence is non-ruling by law, and this covers all incidents lacking certainty, for it is the evidence; so one stays silent or acts on original permissibility according to two opinions, as has passed. The most apparent is permissibility in matters with no legal evidence, so incidents are not devoid. (I say: Moreover, in the legislation of consensus and analogy, there is coverage of most, so there is no emptiness except in the least. But contemplation shows that consensus is on a limited number of incidents, and analogy requires an original to be measured upon, which can only be from Quran, mutawatir Sunnah, or consensus, and these are insufficient, so reflect. And the impossibility of the consequent may be denied rationally, for the impossibility of incidents being devoid of rulings does not appear to reason; it is only by law. But the impossibility appears by clinging to rational good and evil in actions, for they entail the attachment of a ruling from the Lawgiver to them, as is the verification by the verifiers of our teachers, so reflect.
Source pages p. 167

Commentary
This passage opens with a ruling: that knowledge of the obligation to act on khabar al-wahid is necessary because of consensus (ijma') that we must act on the probability (zann) from the apparent meaning of the Quran. The author then presents the Quranic evidence from verse 49:6, which commands investigation upon a report from a sinful person. The Hanafis deduce by mafhum al-mukhalafah (concept of contrary implication) that a report from a just person is to be accepted without investigation. The commentator notes that this deduction relies on mafhum, which some Hanafis (like the Iraqi school) reject. However, the author shows that even if mafhum is weak, the ruling is supported by consensus. The objectors argue that the mafhum of the condition is too broad, but the author clarifies that it is actually mafhum al-sifah (concept of the attribute) that gives the intended meaning: when the reporter is just, accept. Then the passage moves to rational arguments: those who argue from reason that avoiding harm is rationally obligatory, and acting on probable reports of harm is rationally required. The author refutes this by stating that rational obligation is not admitted by all, and that the real obligation is legal. Another rational argument is that if khabar al-wahid were not binding, most incidents would have no rulings. The answer: in the absence of evidence, we apply original permissibility (ibahah asliyyah) or stop. Finally, the author notes that consensus and analogy cover most cases, and the idea of emptiness is baseless. The discussion ends with a reference to rational good and evil as a basis for legal rulings according to some Hanafi verifiers.

Key Terms
مفهوم المخالفة (mafhum al-mukhalafah): The concept of contrary implication: deriving a ruling from the opposite of the mentioned condition or attribute.
خبر الواحد (khabar al-wahid): A report transmitted by a single narrator or a number less than tawatur, which yields probability (zann).
مفهوم الصفة (mafhum al-sifah): The concept of the attribute: the implication that the ruling is tied to a specific attribute, and its opposite applies when the attribute is absent.

Key Terms from Source Passage

According to the passage, what is the main basis for the obligation to act on khabar al-wahid?
A) Quran 49:6 alone
B) Consensus (ijma') that we act on probability from the Quran's apparent meaning
C) Rational necessity
D) The attribute 'fasiq' in the verse

Key Takeaway
The obligation to act on khabar al-wahid is established primarily by consensus (ijma'), with Quranic verse 49:6 providing supporting evidence through the refined concept of mafhum al-sifah.

Refuting Rafidi Objections to Khabar al-Wahid
Refuting two Rafidi objections to khabar al-wahid

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two Rafidi objections to khabar al-wahid and apply the Hanafi refutation to each, distinguishing between a legitimate suspicion and a general rejection of ahad reports.

Core Idea
The Rafidis' own proof refutes them: their evidence against khabar al-wahid is itself probable (zanni).

The Rafidis (a Shi'a sect) reject khabar al-wahid as a source of law, arguing that acting on probability is forbidden and that the Prophet himself hesitated to act on a single report in the Dhul-Yadayn incident. This lesson unpacks their two arguments and the Hanafi responses, showing how the objections are internally contradictory and based on a misinterpretation of the incident. You will see why the Hanafi school upholds khabar al-wahid as a binding proof in legal matters.

Guided Path
1
Understand the First Objection
The Rafidis cite Quran 17:36 and 10:66 to argue that following khabar al-wahid is following probability, which Allah forbids. Recognize the premise: khabar al-wahid is probable (zanni), and the Quran prohibits following probability.
The verses are: 'Do not pursue that of which you have no knowledge' and 'They follow nothing but probability'.
2
Analyze the Hanafi Refutation
The Hanafi response points out that the verses themselves are probable in their indication (dalalah zanniyyah). If they are used to forbid probability, they are self-refuting. Moreover, if the opponent claims the verses are certain, that contradicts their own usul that general texts are probable. This is an ad hominem argument that exposes inconsistency.
The text says: 'فيه إبطال الشيء بنفسه' (it is self-refutation).
3
Understand the Second Objection
The Rafidis cite the incident of Dhul-Yadayn, where the Prophet waited for a second report before acting on the report of forgetfulness in prayer. They claim this shows the Prophet did not accept a single report.
The hadith is narrated by Abu Hurairah and is mutafaq alayh (agreed upon).
4
Analyze the Hanafi Refutation
The Hanafi response has two parts. First, the Dhul-Yadayn report itself is a khabar al-wahid, so it cannot be used to reject khabar al-wahid. Second, the Prophet's hesitation was due to the uniqueness of the reporter (he was alone among a crowd sharing the cause of knowledge), which raised a suspicion of error, not a general principle against ahad reports.
The text says: 'إنما توقف اللريبة لأن الإنفراد من بين جماعة مشاركة في سبب العلم مظنة الكذب'.
5
Synthesize the Hanafi Position
The Rafidi objections fail because they are either self-refuting or misinterpret the evidence. The Hanafi school maintains that khabar al-wahid is a valid proof (hujjah) in legal matters, supported by consensus, Quran 49:6, and the Prophet's consistent practice of acting on ahad reports.
This is a foundational principle in Hanafi usul al-fiqh.

الروافض ومن وافقهم قالوا : (أولاً) التعبد بخبر الواحد اتباع الظن، وقد قال الله تعالى: ﴿وَلَا نَقْفُ مَا لَيْسَ لَكَ بِهِ عِلْم [الإسراء : ٣٦] و : وإن يَتَّبِعُونَ إِلَّا الظَّنَّ [يونس : ٦٦] قلنا :
