The Rafidis and those who agree with them said: First, devotion to khabar al-wahid is following probability, and Allah said: 'Do not pursue that of which you have no knowledge' (17:36) and 'They follow nothing but probability' (10:66). We say: In this is self-refutation, because it is a probable indication and its implication is to invalidate probability. If you say the general is certain, there is no probability, I say this is a refutation and imposition upon them because the general is probable according to them. So these two verses are probable, so acting on them is forbidden, and they are not suitable as evidence. It can also be stated: If it were correct by probability, then acting on these two verses would be correct, but the consequent is false because it negates acting on probability. In this, the entailment is denied, because acting on probability itself does not necessitate acting on it when an impossibility would result from acting on it; acting on a probable does not necessarily entail acting on these two verses. Understand, reflect, and remember what has passed of the solution. (And) they said: Secondly, he (the Prophet) waited, peace be upon him and his family and companions and wives, in the report of Dhul-Yadayn regarding shortening and forgetfulness until another informed him, so he did not act on the single report. And this report about the Messenger of Allah is the same in providing probability. From Muhammad ibn Sirin, from Abu Hurairah: The Messenger of Allah led us in one of the evening prayers—Abu Hurairah named it, but I forgot—so he prayed two rak'ahs and then said salam. He then stood against a piece of wood placed in the mosque, leaned on it, placed his right hand on his left and interlocked his fingers, placed his right cheek on the back of his left hand. The fast people went out through the mosque doors saying: The prayer has been shortened. Among the people were Abu Bakr and Umar, but they feared to speak to him. Among the people was a man with long hands called Dhul-Yadayn. He said: O Messenger of Allah, have you forgotten or has the prayer been shortened? He said: 'I have not forgotten nor has it been shortened.' He said: Is it as Dhul-Yadayn says? They said: Yes. So he stepped forward and prayed what he had missed, then said salam, then said takbir and prostrated like his normal prostration or longer, then raised his head and said takbir and prostrated like his normal prostration or longer, then raised his head and said takbir. Perhaps they asked him, then he said salam. He said: I was told that Imran ibn Husain said: then he said salam. Narrated by al-Bukhari and Muslim. This was before the prohibition of speaking during prayer, as said by Shaykh Abd al-Haqq al-Dehlawi. As for his saying 'I have not forgotten nor has it been shortened,' its meaning is: I have not forgotten in my opinion, nor have I lied, even inadvertently, as said by Imam al-Nawawi as transmitted. Allah knows best the truth. (We say) first, that it is a khabar al-wahid, so it cannot be used to invalidate it. Secondly, he waited only due to doubt, because being alone from among a group sharing in the cause of knowledge is a suspicion of lying, as previously mentioned, not because it is a khabar al-wahid. How, when he has repeatedly acted on ahad reports? So reflect.
Source pages p. 167

Commentary
This passage presents two objections raised by the Rafidis (a Shi'a sect) against the authority of khabar al-wahid, along with the Hanafi responses. First objection: Following khabar al-wahid is acting on probability, which is prohibited by Quranic verses (17:36, 10:66). The response exposes a self-contradiction: those verses themselves are probable in their indication (zanni), so if they were used to forbid probability, they would be self-refuting. Moreover, if the verses were certain for the objectors, that contradicts their own usul that general texts are probable. The second objection: the incident of Dhul-Yadayn, where the Prophet waited for a second report before acting on the report of forgetfulness. The Hanafi response states that this very report is a khabar al-wahid, so it cannot be used to reject khabar al-wahid. Moreover, the Prophet's hesitation was due to the uniqueness of the reporter among a crowd (a suspicion of error), not because it was a single report. The commentary notes that the Prophet frequently acted on ahad reports, as seen in many hadiths. Thus, both objections are invalid.

Key Terms
الروافض (al-rawafid): A sect that rejects the authority of the first three caliphs and much of the Sunni hadith corpus, including khabar al-wahid.
خبر ذي اليدين (khabar dhil-yadayn): The report of Dhul-Yadayn about the Prophet forgetting parts of the prayer, used by opponents to argue against acting on a single report.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Because Dhul-Yadayn was alone among a crowd that shared in the cause of knowledge, raising suspicion of error
C) Because the report concerned a matter of disbelief
D) Because the Prophet was uncertain about his own memory

Key Takeaway
The Rafidi objections to khabar al-wahid fail because their own proof is self-refuting and their interpretation of the Dhul-Yadayn incident is based on a specific circumstance, not a general principle.

Khabar al-Wahid in Hudud: The Hanafi Majority View
Resolving the dispute on khabar al-wahid in hudud

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the majority Hanafi position on the acceptance of khabar al-wahid in hudud and evaluate the argument based on the hadith 'Avert hudud by doubts'.

Core Idea
A just single narrator's report is accepted in hudud; doubt (shubha) does not arise from the report itself.

This passage addresses a key intra-Hanafi dispute: Is a report from a single just narrator sufficient evidence to impose a hadd punishment? The majority, including Abu Yusuf and al-Jassas, say yes, while al-Karkhi and others invoke the famous principle 'Avert hudud by doubts.' We will break down the proof and the counterargument, clarifying the Hanafi position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions
Find the parties: the majority (Abu Yusuf, al-Jassas) who accept khabar al-wahid in hudud, and the opponents (al-Karkhi, al-Basri) who reject it based on shubha.
Note that both are within the Hanafi school, though al-Basri is Mu'tazili.
2
Analyze the majority's proof (dalil)
The proof given: the narrator is just and decisive (عَدْلٌ جَازِمٌ) and reports on a practical ruling (حُكْمٍ عَمَلِيٍّ), so his narration is accepted like any other. Identify the key terms: عدل, جازم, حكم عملي.
The majority relies on the general reliability of the narrator.
3
Understand the objection (shubha)
The opponent argues that hudud are averted by doubts, and a single report creates uncertainty. The text quotes the hadith: 'ادرؤوا الحدود بالشبهات'. Understand how this principle is used to block acceptance.
The hadith is attributed to Imam Abu Hanifa in some narrations.
4
Evaluate the majority's response
The response is that a just report itself removes doubt; the hadith refers to genuine ambiguity, not to clear testimony from a reliable narrator. Recognize that the core issue is whether the report constitutes a shubha.
The text says 'إنما الأهم كشف الشبهة لا غير' emphasizing that identifying the shubha is crucial.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
What is the practical difference? In a case where a single just witness reports a hudud crime, the majority would impose the penalty, while al-Karkhi would not. Consider the implications for evidence law.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة: (عند الجمهور خبر (الواحد العدل (مقبول في الحدود وهو قول الإمام أبي (يوسف) رحمه الله تعالى عليه (والشيخ أبي بكر (الجصاص) الرازي (خلافاً للكرخي) الشيخ أبي الحسن من الحنفية والبصري) من المعتزلة وأكثر (الحنفية على ما في «التحرير» (لنا) الراوي (عدل) جازم) روي (في) حكم ( عملي فيقبل) روايته (كغيره) أي كما يقبل في غير من العمليات ولعلك تقول : الخصم لا يسلم القبول في كل عملي، بل فيما إذا لم يمنع مانع، وههنا الشبهة مانعة عنده، والمقصود واضح، فإن خبر الواحد مفيد لحكم الله تعالى، فيجب العمل به وهذا واضح إنما الأهم كشف الشبهة لا غير فافهم، الإمام الكرخي وأتباعه (قالوا : قال عليه وعلى آله وأصحابه وأهل بيته الصلاة والسلام) من الله تعالى العزيز العلام (ادرؤوا الحدود بالشبهات رواه الإمام أبو حنيفة رضي الله عنه ومثله في بعض السنن
Issue: According to the majority (jumhur), a single just narrator's report is accepted in hudud; this is the saying of Imam Abu Yusuf (may Allah have mercy on him) and Shaykh Abi Bakr al-Jassas al-Razi, contrary to al-Karkhi (Shaykh Abi al-Hasan from the Hanafis) and al-Basri from the Mu'tazila, and most Hanafis according to 'al-Tahrir'. Our proof: The narrator is just and decisive, he narrates regarding a practical ruling, so his narration is accepted like other practical matters. You might say: The opponent does not concede acceptance in every practical matter, but rather where there is no preventer; here, the doubt (shubha) is a preventer in their view. The intent is clear: the khabar al-wahid conveys the ruling of Allah, so acting on it is obligatory, and this is obvious; the important thing is to uncover the doubt, nothing else, so understand. Imam al-Karkhi and his followers said: He said (peace be upon him and his family and companions and household): 'Avert hudud by doubts' narrated by Imam Abu Hanifah (may Allah be pleased with him) and similar in some Sunan.
Source pages p. 168

Commentary
This passage addresses a specific dispute within the Hanafi school about the acceptance of khabar al-wahid in matters of hudud (fixed corporal punishments). The majority position, held by Abu Yusuf and al-Jassas, is that a report from a single just narrator is accepted in hudud, just like in any other practical ruling. The opposing view, attributed to al-Karkhi (a prominent Hanafi usuli) and al-Basri (Mu'tazili), is that hudud are averted by doubts, so a single report, being less than certainty, is not sufficient. The commentary explains the majority proof: the narrator is just and reports a ruling, so it should be accepted; the doubt (shubha) that al-Karkhi invokes is not inherent in the report but is an external consideration. The passage ends by quoting the hadith 'Avert hudud by doubts' as evidence for the opposing view, but the context implies that the majority still holds that a just report does not constitute a doubt that would avert the hadd. The issue is thus resolved by affirming the general principle of accepting just reports unless a specific shubha exists.

Key Terms
الحدود (al-hudud): Fixed punishments prescribed by Shariah for certain major sins, e.g., theft, zina.
الشبهة (al-shubha): A doubt or ambiguity that prevents the application of a hadd punishment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority view in the text, why is khabar al-wahid accepted in hudud?
A) Because hudud are not serious punishments
B) Because the narrator is just and reports a practical ruling, so it should be accepted like other rulings
C) Because the hadith 'Avert hudud by doubts' is weak
D) Because the report is certain

Key Takeaway
The majority Hanafi view accepts khabar al-wahid in hudud, as a just narrator's report does not constitute a doubt that would avert the penalty.

Refuting the Dhu al-Yadayn Objection: The Hanafi Defense of Khabar Wahid
Hanafi refutation of an objection to khabar wahid.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two Hanafi responses to the Dhu al-Yadayn objection and evaluate why the Prophet's hesitation does not undermine the acceptance of khabar wahid.

Core Idea
Prophet's hesitation was due to being alone among a group, not because khabar wahid is rejected.

The opponents of khabar wahid often cite the hadith of Dhu al-Yadayn, where the Prophet (صلى الله عليه وآله) hesitated upon hearing a single companion's report. They claim this proves that a solitary report is not a valid proof. However, the Hanafi school offers a two-pronged refutation: first, the very hadith used as evidence is itself a khabar wahid and cannot be used to overturn established usul principles; second, the Prophet's hesitation was due to his unique position as the sole individual making a claim contrary to a gathered congregation, a situation that raises suspicion of error or forgetfulness, not a general ruling on solitary reports. This lesson unpacks the reasoning behind this refutation.

Guided Path
1
Understand the Objection
Identify the opponent's claim: the Prophet hesitated upon hearing from Dhu al-Yadayn, so he did not accept a single report. Recognize that this is used to argue that khabar wahid is not a valid proof.
2
First Hanafi Response: Methodological Self-Refutation
The hadith itself is a khabar wahid (reported by a single chain). If the opponents use it to reject khabar wahid, they are using the very type of evidence they seek to invalidate. This is a circular argument.
A khabar wahid cannot be used as definitive proof against the acceptance of other ahad reports.
3
Second Hanafi Response: Context of the Hesitation
The Prophet's hesitation was not due to the number of reporters but because he was alone among a large group in claiming the prayer had not been shortened. Being alone among many is a cause of suspicion of falsehood (mazinnat al-kadhib), as earlier usul principles state.
The hesitation is a precautionary measure, not a rejection of the mode of transmission.
4
Confirmatory Evidence: Prophet's Practice
The Prophet repeatedly acted upon single reports (akhad ahad) in other instances, proving that he accepted khabar wahid. The Dhu al-Yadayn incident is an exception based on a different cause.
Consider examples like accepting the report of one person about the sighting of the crescent moon.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقالوا :(ثانياً : توقف عليه وعلى آله وأصحابه وأزواجه الصلاة والسلام في خبر ذي اليدين) بالقصر والنسيان (حتى أخبر غيره) فلم يعمل بخبر الواحد، وهذا والخبر عن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم سواء في إفادة الظن عن محمد بن سيرين قدس الله سره العزيز عن أبي هريرة رضي الله تعالى عنه صلى بنا رسول الله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم أحد صلاتي العشاء قد سماها أبو هريرة، لكن نسيت فصلى بنا ركعتين ثم سلم فقام إلى خشبة معروضة في المسجد فاتكأ عليها، ووضع يده اليمنى على اليسرى وشبك بين أصابعه، ووضع خده الأيمن على ظهر كفه اليسرى، وخرجت سرعان الناس من أبواب المسجد فقالوا : قصرت الصلاة، وفي القوم أبو بكر وعمر فهاباه أن يكلماه وفي القوم رجل في يده طول يقال له : ذو اليدين فقال يا رسول الله أنسيت أم قصرت الصلاة؟ فقال: «لم أنس ولم تقصر» فقال : أكما يقول ذو اليدين؟ فقالوا: نعم، فتقدم وصلى ما ترك ثم سلم ثم كبر وسجد مثل سجوده أو أطول، ثم رفع رأسه وكبر وسجد مثل سجوده أو أطول، ثم رفع رأسه وكبر، فربما سألوه ثم سلم، فقال نبئت أن عمران بن حصين قال : ثم سلم رواه الشيخان وهذا كان قبل تحريم التكلم في الصلاة، كذا قال الشيخ عبد الحق الدهلوي، وأما قوله : لم أنس ولم تقصر» فمعناه : لم أنس في ظني ولا كذب فيه ولو سهواً كذا قال الإمام النووي على ما نقل هو والله أعلم بالصواب (قلنا) أولاً إنه خبر الواحد فلا يستدل به لإبطاله وثانياً : إنما توقف اللريبة لأن الإنفراد من بين جماعة) مشاركة في سبب العلم مظنة الكذب كما تقدم، لا لأنه خبر الواحد كيف، وقد عمل مراراً بخبر الآحاد فتدبر .
And they said: Secondly, he (the Prophet) hesitated upon the report of Dhu al-Yadayn, until another informed him, so he did not act upon the report of one. And this report from the Messenger of Allah is equal in producing zann. From Muhammad ibn Sirin from Abu Hurairah: The Messenger of Allah led us in one of the evening prayers... then he said: 'I did not forget and the prayer was not shortened.' He asked: 'Is it as Dhu al-Yadayn says?' They said: 'Yes.' Then he advanced and prayed what he had missed... So their objection. We say: First, it is a khabar wahid, so it cannot be used to refute it. Second, he hesitated only due to doubt because his being alone among a group is a shared cause of knowledge and a cause for suspicion of falsehood, as stated earlier, not because it is a khabar wahid. He had repeatedly acted upon ahad reports, so reflect.
Source pages p. 168

Commentary
This passage presents the second objection raised by opponents of khabar wahid: the famous hadith of Dhu al-Yadayn, where the Prophet (صلى الله عليه وآله) upon being informed by a single companion that he had prayed only two rak'ahs, hesitated until others confirmed. The objection claims that this shows the Prophet did not accept the report of a single individual. The Hanafi response is twofold: first, that this hadith itself is a khabar wahid and thus cannot be used to invalidate other khabar wahid. Second, the Prophet's hesitation was not due to the number of reporters but because he was alone among a large group in claiming something contrary to the apparent state. Being alone among a group is a cause of suspicion of falsehood (mazinnat al-kadhib), not the nature of khabar wahid. The Hanafis emphasize that the Prophet repeatedly acted upon single reports (akhad ahad) in other instances.

Key Terms
خبر الواحد (khabar al-wahid): A report from one or two individuals that does not reach tawatur and provides probabilistic knowledge (zann).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi response, why did the Prophet hesitate upon receiving Dhu al-Yadayn's report?
A) Because khabar wahid is not a valid proof.
B) Because he was alone among a group, raising suspicion of falsehood.
C) Because he forgot the prayer.
D) Because he was testing Dhu al-Yadayn's honesty.

Key Takeaway
The Dhu al-Yadayn hadith does not undermine the acceptance of khabar wahid; the Prophet's hesitation was context-specific and not a general rule.

Hanafi Defense of Khabar al-Wahid for Hudud
Hanafi responses to objections against using khabar al-wahid for hudud

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and explain the three Hanafi responses to the objection that khabar al-wahid cannot establish hadd punishments due to shubha, and evaluate the strength of each rebuttal.

Core Idea
Shubha preventing hudud is only in the cause, not in the established ruling; thus khabar al-wahid is valid.

This passage presents a Hanafi usul dispute defending the use of khabar al-wahid for hadd punishments. Opponents invoke the hadith 'avert hudud by shubha' to argue that khabar al-wahid, being zanni, contains shubha. The Hanafi response is threefold: (1) shubha before binding vs. after, (2) refutation by analogy to shahada and zahir al-kitab, (3) appeal to khabar mashhur providing tranquility. We will analyze each argument and its counter-rebuttal.

Guided Path
1
Identify the opponent's objection
The opponent claims that khabar al-wahid contains shubha (doubt) and therefore cannot be used for hadd punishments, citing the principle 'avert hudud by shubha'.
This is a common usul dispute between Hanafis and others (e.g., Shafi'is) over the threshold of certainty required for hudud.
2
Examine the first Hanafi response
Hanafis distinguish shubha before the ruling becomes binding (in the establishment of the cause) from shubha after. The hadith applies only to the former; shubha in the proof (dalil) does not prevent, just as in other practical matters.
The key is the timing of shubha relative to the binding of the hadd.
3
Analyze the second response and counter-refutations
The Hanafis rebut by pointing out that shahada (testimony) also contains shubha but is accepted – however, it is ta'abbudi and not analogized. Similarly, zahir al-kitab (apparent meaning of Quran) is zanni but used for hudud. Opponents counter that the Quran's generality is specified, making it zanni, but Hanafis argue specification by an independent text is rare.
These refutations (naqd) show consistency in Hanafi methodology.
4
Understand the third response: khabar mashhur
Hanafis also argue that khabar mashhur (well-known report) contains shubha but is accepted because it provides tranquility (tuma'nina). Shubha not arising from a proof is disregarded.
Khabar mashhur is stronger than khabar al-wahid, but the same principle applies.
5
Evaluate the overall strength of the Hanafi position
The three responses collectively defend the validity of khabar al-wahid for hudud. The distinctions (shubha timing, ta'abbud, tranquility) are methodologically consistent within Hanafi usul.
Consider whether the opponents' counter-rebuttals (e.g., specification of Quranic verses) undermine the Hanafi argument fully.

أيضاً (وفيه) أي خبر الواحد (شبهة) فلا يقتل في الحدود قلنا: أولاً، المراد درء الحد بالشبهة قبل اللزوم والمعنى : ادرؤوا الحدود بإحداث الشبهات في ثبوت سبب الحدد (لا) الدرء بالشبهة في الحد اللازم) يعني الشبهة في دليل ثبوت الحكم المثبت في الذمة، فإنها غير مانعة، كما في سائر العمليات وعلى هذا فالاستدلال بهذا الوجه على عدم إثبات الحد بالقياس لا يتم، بل يستدل عليه بعدم اهتداء العقل إلى التقديرات الشرعية إن تم (و) قلنا (ثانياً) دليلكم (منقوض بالشهادة لأن فيه شبهة أيضاً، فلا يقبل بل فيه شبهة في ثبوت السبب، والجواب عنه : أن أمر الشهادة تعبدي على خلاف القياس، فلا يقاس عليه (و) منقوض بـ (ظاهر الكتاب) فإنه ظني أيضاً، فلا يصلح إثباته للحدود (وربما يتخلص عن النقضين (بأن التعبد بالشهادة بالنص) القطعي فيخص به ظاهر الخبر وظاهر الكتاب قطعي) وليس فيه شبهة الانتفاء الاحتمال الناشيء عن دليل وهو المعتبر لا مجرد الاحتمال فافهم، وقد يدفع هذا الجواب بأن العموم الوارد في آيات الحدود مخصوص وهو ظني اتفاقاً، وهذا إنما يتم لو كان للتخصيص بالكلام المستقل الملاصق وإثباته خرط القتاد وقلنا ثالثاً : إنه منقوض بالخبر المشهور إذ فيه شبهة أيضاً، وجوابه بأنه مفيد للطمأنينة والشبهة بعدها غير معتبرة لعدم انتشائها عن دليل (فافهم).
Also (in it) meaning khabar al-wahid (there is shubha) so he is not killed in hudud. We say: First, the meaning of averting the hadd by shubha is before binding, and the meaning is: avert the hudud by creating shubha in the establishment of the cause of the hadd, (not) averting by shubha in the established hadd. Meaning, shubha in the proof of the ruling established in the dhimmah, it is not a preventer, as in all other practical matters. And upon this, the inference by this point on the non-establishment of hadd by qiyas is not complete, rather it is inferred by the intellect not being guided to the shar'i estimations, if it is complete. (And) we said (secondly) your proof (is refuted by shahada because there is also shubha in it, so it should not be accepted, rather there is shubha in the establishment of the cause. And the answer to it: that the matter of shahada is ta'abbudi against qiyas, so it is not analogized upon it. (And) it is refuted by (zahir al-kitab) because it is also zanni, so it is not suitable for establishing hudud. (And perhaps one may be saved from the two refutations (by saying that the ta'abbud in shahada is by a qat'i text) so khabar's zahir and kitab's zahir are qat'i, and there is no shubha of non-existence, the probability arising from a proof is what is considered, not mere probability, so understand. And this answer may be rebutted: that the generalities in the verses of hudud are specified and are zanni by agreement, and this is only complete if the specification is by an independent adjacent speech, and its establishment is extremely difficult. And we said thirdly: it is refuted by khabar mashhur, for there is shubha in it also. The answer to it: that it gives tranquility and shubha after it is not considered because it does not arise from a proof. (So understand).
Source pages p. 169

Commentary
This passage presents a Hanafi usul dispute. The opponents argue that khabar al-wahid (single-narrator report) contains shubha (doubt), so it cannot be used to establish hadd punishments, per the principle 'avert hudud by shubha'. The Hanafi response is threefold. First, the principle applies before the hadd becomes binding, not after; the shubha here is in the proof of the cause, not in the established hadd, and such shubha does not prevent, as in other practical matters. Therefore, the argument against using qiyas for hudud fails. Second, the opponents' proof is refuted by shahada (testimony) which also has shubha but is accepted; but that is ta'abbudi (based on textual command) and not subject to analogy. Similarly, zahir al-kitab (apparent meaning of the Quran) is zanni but accepted; the reply that the Quran's apparent meaning is qat'i here is rebutted because the general verses on hudud are specified and thus zanni. Third, the argument is refuted by khabar mashhur (well-known report) which also has shubha but is accepted because it provides tranquility, and shubha not arising from a proof is disregarded. The passage thus defends the Hanafi position that khabar al-wahid is valid for establishing hudud.

Key Terms
شبهة (shubha): Doubt or ambiguity that may prevent a legal ruling, specifically in the proof of the cause of a ruling.
خبر واحد (khabar al-wahid): A report transmitted by a single narrator or a limited chain that does not reach tawatur.
حد (hadd): A fixed punishment prescribed by Islamic law for certain offenses (e.g., theft, adultery).
ظاهر الكتاب (zahir al-kitab): The apparent meaning of the Quranic text, which may be zanni (probable) unless specified.
خبر مشهور (khabar mashhur): A report transmitted by at least three narrators in each generation, widely known but not reaching tawatur.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi response, what is the correct interpretation of 'avert hudud by shubha'?
A) It applies even after the hadd becomes binding.
B) It applies before the hadd becomes binding, specifically to shubha in the cause.
C) It applies only to shubha in the narrators.
D) It applies to all shubha without distinction.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school accepts khabar al-wahid for hudud because only shubha in the cause before binding prevents, not shubha in the proof of the ruling.

The Hanafi Classification of Reports (Khabar) by Subject
Hanafi division of khabar into rights of Allah and rights of slaves

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify a report according to its subject (huquq Allah vs huquq al-'ibad) and identify the acceptance conditions for each category, including exceptions.

Core Idea
The conditions for accepting a report vary by subject: justice for divine rights, number and wording for impositions, discernment alone for gifts.

In Hanafi usul, not all reports (khabar) are treated equally. The School classifies reports based on their subject matter into the rights of Allah (huquq Allah) and the rights of slaves (huquq al-'ibad). Within the latter, further distinctions are made based on whether the report involves a pure legal claim (ilzam mahd), no claim at all, or a claim from some respects. This classification determines the conditions for accepting a report, from requiring full shahada conditions to merely requiring discernment (tamyiz). Understanding this classification is essential for correctly applying hadith and witness testimony in different contexts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two primary divisions of reports
The passage divides reports into those concerning huquq Allah (punishments and acts of worship) and huquq al-'ibad (transactions and claims). The first line of the passage states this division.
2
Examine the condition for huquq Allah
For huquq Allah, a just ('adl) reporter is required; a fasiq's report is not accepted. The passage illustrates this with the example of water purity: if a just person reports impurity, tayammum is allowed; if a fasiq reports, one must do taharri.
This shows that in divine matters, the reporter's integrity ('adala) is paramount.
3
Analyze the three subcategories of huquq al-'ibad
The passage splits huquq al-'ibad into: (a) pure imposition (ilzam mahd), e.g., sales when one denies; (b) no imposition at all, e.g., wakala and gifts; (c) imposition from some respects and not others, e.g., dismissal of a wakil.
The subdivision is based on the presence and nature of a legal claim (ilzam).
4
Determine the conditions for each subcategory
For (a): requires wilaya, wording of shahada, number (two men or one man + two women). Exceptions: midwife (no number/male required due to necessity) and testimony against a kafir (no Islam condition). For (b): only tamyiz and tasdiq al-qalb (believing the reporter) are required. For (c): the original party (wakil or messenger) is accepted even if fasiq or slave; but a third party (fuduli) requires number or justice according to Imam Muhammad, while the two companions require only tamyiz and tasdiq al-qalb (the text says the latter is preferred).
The ikhtilaf on the third party will be explored further in a dedicated lesson.
5
Apply to examples from the passage
The passage gives examples: if a just person reports water impurity, tayammum is permitted; if a fasiq reports water impurity, one does taharri. A slave girl's report of a gift is accepted with tasdiq al-qalb. A midwife's testimony is accepted without number or male condition.
These examples illustrate how the classification works in practice.

A division according to the Hanafis: (The locus of the report absolutely) from the restriction of it being a report from the Messenger of Allah, his family and companions (is either the rights of Allah Almighty, which are punishments or acts of worship and transactions, and it) meaning the just single narrator (is a proof in both) meaning punishments and acts of worship, like the report of the purity or impurity of water. So if a just person reports its impurity, tayammum is permitted. And the report from the Messenger of Allah, his family and companions: its ruling is obligation, and it is worship (as passed). And the report of a fasiq is not accepted in them, so tayammum is not allowed by the report of a fasiq about water's impurity, rather one acts by taharri. If the taharri falls on that it is pure, he performs wudu, and combining tayammum is preferred. If it falls on impurity, he performs tayammum and spilling the water is preferred. (And as for the rights of slaves) it is either pure imposition, or there is no imposition at all, or it has imposition from some respects and not from others. (So what involves pure imposition like sales when one of the two denies (and similar) like other claims, then alongside the conditions of riwaya, wilaya is required: the statement of a disbeliever against a Muslim is not accepted, nor the statement of a slave, and the wording of shahada, and number, and that the reporters be two men or two women with one man when possible. And it is authentically reported from the Messenger of Allah, his family and companions that he accepted the testimony of the midwife. And there is no requirement of Islam in testimony against a disbeliever, because a Muslim rarely witnesses the transactions of disbelievers, so there is also necessity. So if a slave girl comes and reports that my master sent me to you as a gift, her statement is accepted and sexual intercourse with her is permissible, (to avoid hardship). For if justice were required, the matter of livelihood would be disrupted, because a person rarely finds a just person to deal with or sends witnesses with gifts. And the Prophet, peace and blessings be upon him and his family, used to accept the report of gifts from the righteous and the wicked, the free and the slave. Indeed, he accepted the gift of Salman when he was a Christian slave. (And what involves imposition from some respects and not from others, like the dismissal of a wakil and the interdiction of a ma'dhun and similar, for this report strips the reporter of established authority and does not entail any claim. So the wakil and messenger of the dismisser and interdictor (as previously) their statement is accepted even if they are fasiq or slave, because they stand in the place of the principal and sender, so their statement is his statement. (And Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani conditioned (in the reporter who is a third party) one of the two aspects of shahada: number or (justice, because when he has two aspects, he acts by both, so he gives the ruling of each from some respects. So if the wakil acts after the report of a single fasiq, his action is valid. (Contrary to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani?), for they say that he is like the first: nothing is required except tamyiz and tasdiq al-qalb due to necessity. We say: necessity is removed by the lack of condition in the messenger and wakil, so consider. And the more apparent is their view. (And regarding the obligation of the shari'ah on one who becomes Muslim in dar al-harb by the report of a single fasiq or disbeliever, there is disagreement. It is said: justice is required because it is a religious matter. And it is said: it is upon the disagreement between the Imam and his two companions as in the third division. And it is said: the most correct is the lack of condition of justice of the reporter (by agreement, so that acts of worship become obligatory upon him, and qada is obligatory if he does not perform them by the report of a fasiq. And this is what Shams al-A'imma said. (Because) the reporter (is the messenger of the messenger) and nothing is required in the report of a messenger. (And it is refuted by riwaya, for the hadith narrator is also the messenger of the messenger. The truth is that the lack of condition is only for the message of a specific man for a specific thing, so justice was not considered in transactions, and it does not follow from that absolute absence. And the truth in inference is that the condition was not considered here because of great hardship, for the arrival of a just person here is rarely possible, so if the statement of the fasiq and disbeliever were not accepted and he were allowed to not perform the acts of worship, that Muslim would not attain human perfection and would resemble animals. So understand that.
Source pages p. 169

Commentary
This passage is a Hanafi classification of reports (khabar) according to their subject matter and the conditions for their acceptance. It first divides reports into those concerning the rights of Allah (huquq Allah) which include punishments ('uqubat) and acts of worship ('ibadat), and those concerning the rights of slaves (huquq al-'ibad) which include transactions (mu'amalat). For the rights of Allah, khabar al-wahid of a just (adl) narrator is a proof (hujja); a fasiq's report is not accepted, and if a fasiq reports impurity of water, one must perform taharri (investigation). For the rights of slaves, there are three subcategories: (1) pure imposition (ilzam mahd) like sales when one denies: requires wilaya, lfadh al-shahada, number (two men or one man and two women), etc. Exceptions: midwife testimony (no male) and testimony against a disbeliever (no Islam requirement due to necessity). (2) No imposition (like wakala, gifts): only tamyiz (discernment) and tasdiq al-qalb (believing the reporter) are needed, because requiring justice would cause hardship. (3) Partial imposition (e.g., dismissal of wakil): the report is accepted even from a fasiq or slave. Then the text discusses the ikhtilaf between Imam Muhammad (who required number or justice for a third-party reporter) and the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani?) who require only tamyiz and tasdiq al-qalb due to necessity; the latter view is preferred. Finally, there is a discussion about the obligation of shari'ah on a new Muslim in dar al-harb upon the report of a fasiq or kafir; the correct view is that justice is not required because of great hardship, and the reporter is like a messenger of the Messenger.

Key Terms
حقوق الله (huquq Allah): Matters pertaining to divine rights: punishments and acts of worship.
إلزام محض (ilzam mahd): Pure imposition: a legal claim that imposes an obligation without any counter-benefit, e.g., sales when one party denies.
تصديق القلب (tasdiq al-qalb): Internal verification that the reporter is truthful; required instead of 'adala in cases of necessity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In cases of pure imposition (ilzam mahd) like sales, what extra conditions are required beyond the general conditions of riwaya?
A) Only tamyiz and tasdiq al-qalb.
B) Wilaya, lfadh al-shahada, number (two men or one man & two women).
C) Only justice ('adala).
D) No extra conditions.

Key Takeaway
The acceptance conditions of a report in Hanafi usul are not uniform; they vary based on whether the report concerns divine rights, pure claims, or non-claims, reflecting the principle of necessity (dharura).

The Hanafi Ikhtilaf on Third-Party Reports and dar al-Harb
Intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on third-party reports and dar al-Harb

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ikhtilaf on the conditions for accepting the report of a third party (fuduli) in matters like wakala, and derive the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) for the validity of actions taken after such a report.

Core Idea
The two companions require only tamyiz for a third party's report due to necessity; Imam Muhammad requires number or justice, but the preferred view is the companions'.

Within the Hanafi school, there is a notable ikhtilaf regarding the report of a third party (fuduli) in matters that have partial imposition, such as the dismissal of a wakil. Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani holds that such a reporter must have either number (two reporters) or justice (one just reporter), because he has two aspects. His two main students, Abu Yusuf and the other Muhammad, argue that only tamyiz and internal verification (tasdiq al-qalb) are needed, due to necessity. This disagreement has practical implications for the validity of actions taken after hearing a single fasiq's report. The passage also extends this discussion to the case of a new Muslim in dar al-harb.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue
The issue is the conditions for accepting the report of a third party (fuduli) regarding the dismissal of a wakil or similar partial imposition. The reporter is not the original party (the wakil himself) but an outsider.
This is distinct from the report of the original wakil, which is always accepted.
2
State Imam Muhammad's position and dalil
Imam Muhammad requires one of the two aspects of shahada: number (two reporters) or justice (one just reporter). His dalil: the reporter has two aspects (shabahain) so gives the ruling of both.
The two aspects are presumably being like a witness and like a mere informant.
3
State the two companions' position and dalil
They require only tamyiz and tasdiq al-qalb, no number/justice, due to necessity. They liken the third party to a messenger or wakil.
Their view is that requiring more would cause hardship.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response and tarjih
The text rebuts: 'Necessity is removed by the lack of condition in the messenger and wakil, so consider. And the more apparent is their view.' Thus the preferred view is the two companions' position.
So the mufta bihi is the easier position.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
If a single fasiq reports the dismissal of a wakil, according to Imam Muhammad the report is not accepted (requires number/justice), so the wakil's subsequent actions are invalid. According to the two, the report is accepted (only tamyiz needed), so the wakil's actions are valid.
This is the practical difference in ruling.
6
Extend to dar al-harb case
The passage discusses whether a report of a fasiq or kafir is accepted to impose shari'ah obligations on a new Muslim. The correct view is that justice is not required due to extreme hardship, and the reporter is like a messenger of the Messenger.
This is analogized to the third-party case but with even stronger necessity.

يقبل قول الفاسق والكافر فيه وجوز عدم الإتيان بالعبادات لم ينل ذلك المسلم الكمال الإنساني، ويلحق بالبهائم فافهم ذلك .
A division according to the Hanafis: (The locus of the report absolutely) from the restriction of it being a report from the Messenger of Allah, his family and companions (is either the rights of Allah Almighty, which are punishments or acts of worship and transactions, and it) meaning the just single narrator (is a proof in both) meaning punishments and acts of worship, like the report of the purity or impurity of water. So if a just person reports its impurity, tayammum is permitted. And the report from the Messenger of Allah, his family and companions: its ruling is obligation, and it is worship (as passed). And the report of a fasiq is not accepted in them, so tayammum is not allowed by the report of a fasiq about water's impurity, rather one acts by taharri. If the taharri falls on that it is pure, he performs wudu, and combining tayammum is preferred. If it falls on impurity, he performs tayammum and spilling the water is preferred. (And as for the rights of slaves) it is either pure imposition, or there is no imposition at all, or it has imposition from some respects and not from others. (So what involves pure imposition like sales when one of the two denies (and similar) like other claims, then alongside the conditions of riwaya, wilaya is required: the statement of a disbeliever against a Muslim is not accepted, nor the statement of a slave, and the wording of shahada, and number, and that the reporters be two men or two women with one man when possible. So there is no number nor male condition in the testimony of the midwife regarding birth, because a man is not present with her, so it is dropped. And it is authentically reported from the Messenger of Allah, his family and companions that he accepted the testimony of the midwife. And there is no requirement of Islam in testimony against a disbeliever, because a Muslim rarely witnesses the transactions of disbelievers, so there is also necessity. And there is the disagreement of al-Shafi'i, may Allah have mercy on him. (And what involves no imposition at all (like wakala, gifts, and similar, and among them reports about meat sold in the markets being the slaughter of a Muslim or a Kitabi, then only tamyiz is required: the statement of a non-discerning child, a non-discerning imbecile, and a madman is not accepted, but the statement of a discerning one is accepted (with tasdiq al-qalb regarding the truthfulness of the reporter. So if a slave girl comes and reports that my master sent me to you as a gift, her statement is accepted and sexual intercourse with her is permissible, (to avoid hardship). For if justice were required, the matter of livelihood would be disrupted, because a person rarely finds a just person to deal with or sends witnesses with gifts. And the Prophet, peace and blessings be upon him and his family, used to accept the report of gifts from the righteous and the wicked, the free and the slave. Indeed, he accepted the gift of Salman when he was a Christian slave. (And what involves imposition from some respects and not from others, like the dismissal of a wakil and the interdiction of a ma'dhun and similar, for this report strips the reporter of established authority and does not entail any claim. So the wakil and messenger of the dismisser and interdictor (as previously) their statement is accepted even if they are fasiq or slave, because they stand in the place of the principal and sender, so their statement is his statement. (And Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani conditioned (in the reporter who is a third party) one of the two aspects of shahada: number or (justice, because when he has two aspects, he acts by both, so he gives the ruling of each from some respects. So if the wakil acts after the report of a single fasiq, his action is valid. (Contrary to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani?), for they say that he is like the first: nothing is required except tamyiz and tasdiq al-qalb due to necessity. We say: necessity is removed by the lack of condition in the messenger and wakil, so consider. And the more apparent is their view. (And regarding the obligation of the shari'ah on one who becomes Muslim in dar al-harb by the report of a single fasiq or disbeliever, there is disagreement. It is said: justice is required because it is a religious matter. And it is said: it is upon the disagreement between the Imam and his two companions as in the third division. And it is said: the most correct is the lack of condition of justice of the reporter (by agreement, so that acts of worship become obligatory upon him, and qada is obligatory if he does not perform them by the report of a fasiq. And this is what Shams al-A'imma said. (Because) the reporter (is the messenger of the messenger) and nothing is required in the report of a messenger. (And it is refuted by riwaya, for the hadith narrator is also the messenger of the messenger. The truth is that the lack of condition is only for the message of a specific man for a specific thing, so justice was not considered in transactions, and it does not follow from that absolute absence. And the truth in inference is that the condition was not considered here because of great hardship, for the arrival of a just person here is rarely possible, so if the statement of the fasiq and disbeliever were not accepted and he were allowed to not perform the acts of worship, that Muslim would not attain human perfection and would resemble animals. So understand that.
Source pages p. 169

Commentary
This passage is a Hanafi classification of reports (khabar) according to their subject matter and the conditions for their acceptance. It first divides reports into those concerning the rights of Allah (huquq Allah) which include punishments ('uqubat) and acts of worship ('ibadat), and those concerning the rights of slaves (huquq al-'ibad) which include transactions (mu'amalat). For the rights of Allah, khabar al-wahid of a just (adl) narrator is a proof (hujja); a fasiq's report is not accepted, and if a fasiq reports impurity of water, one must perform taharri (investigation). For the rights of slaves, there are three subcategories: (1) pure imposition (ilzam mahd) like sales when one denies: requires wilaya, lfadh al-shahada, number (two men or one man and two women), etc. Exceptions: midwife testimony (no male) and testimony against a disbeliever (no Islam requirement due to necessity). (2) No imposition (like wakala, gifts): only tamyiz (discernment) and tasdiq al-qalb (believing the reporter) are needed, because requiring justice would cause hardship. (3) Partial imposition (e.g., dismissal of wakil): the report is accepted even from a fasiq or slave. Then the text discusses the ikhtilaf between Imam Muhammad (who required number or justice for a third-party reporter) and the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani?) who require only tamyiz and tasdiq al-qalb due to necessity; the latter view is preferred. Finally, there is a discussion about the obligation of shari'ah on a new Muslim in dar al-harb upon the report of a fasiq or kafir; the correct view is that justice is not required because of great hardship, and the reporter is like a messenger of the Messenger.

Key Terms
حقوق الله (huquq Allah): Matters pertaining to divine rights: punishments and acts of worship.
إلزام محض (ilzam mahd): Pure imposition: a legal claim that imposes an obligation without any counter-benefit, e.g., sales when one party denies.
تصديق القلب (tasdiq al-qalb): Internal verification that the reporter is truthful; required instead of 'adala in cases of necessity.
فضولي (fuduli): A third party who reports a matter not directly concerning his own rights; e.g., someone other than the wakil reporting dismissal.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred view in the Hanafi school, what is the minimum condition for accepting the report of a third party (fuduli) regarding the dismissal of a wakil?
A) Justice and number.
B) Only tamyiz and tasdiq al-qalb.
C) Two male witnesses.
D) The reporter must be the wakil himself.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school prefers the view that a third party's report in matters of partial imposition requires only tamyiz and tasdiq al-qalb due to necessity, making it acceptable even from a single fasiq.

Minimum Age for Tamyiz in Hadith Transmission
Debate on the minimum age for tamyiz for hadith transmission.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position that tamyiz is not determined by a fixed age and evaluate the evidence for varying opinions.

Core Idea
Tamyiz is not bound by a specific age — it is an individual intellectual capacity.

The transmission of hadith requires that the narrator possesses intellect and discernment (tamyiz) at the time of hearing. Scholars debated the minimum age at which this capacity typically appears. This lesson examines the main opinions and the preferred Hanafi view that no fixed age can be set, as intellectual growth varies by divine mercy.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition for tahammul
The text states that intellect and tamyiz are conditions for receiving hadith (tahammul). Recognize that without tamyiz, the hearing is not valid for transmission.
Tamyiz means discernment — understanding what is said, not just memorizing sounds.
2
List the three opinions on minimum age
The text presents three opinions: five years (Ibn al-Salah), four years (variant of the same hadith), and fifteen years (Ibn Ma'in). Note the evidence for each.
Opinions are based on the hadith of Mahmud ibn al-Rabi' or general reasoning.
3
Analyze the hadith evidence
The hadith 'I understood the spittle... at age five' is used to support age five, but a variant claims Mahmud was four. Understand that an individual incident does not establish a general minimum.
The hadith is ahad (zanni) and its dalala is limited.
4
Understand the rejection of fixed age estimation
The text argues that all fixed estimates 'do not deserve attention' because intelligence strengthens gradually and varies. The 'most correct' view is no estimation by age.
This is the Hanafi position: tamyiz is determined case by case.
5
Apply the principle of individual variation
In practice, a child's tamyiz is assessed by their ability to understand and respond appropriately, not by reaching a specific birthday.
This aligns with the Hanafi emphasis on actual capacity over arbitrary limits.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مقدمة : في شرائط الرواية (فمنها التعقل) والتمييز (للتحمل) أي لتحمل الحديث، وقد اختلفوا في تعيين أقل السنين التي يحصل بها التمييز فقيل : خمسة، وهو المختار عند ابن الصلاح، كما قال محمود بن الربيع : عقلت مجة مجها رسول الله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم وأنا ابن خمس سنين رواه البخاري وقيل أربعة لحديث المجة وزعم هذا القائل بأن الصحيح أن محمود بن الربيع كان هذا الحديث أنه لا يكون الأقل المجة ابن أربع في الصحيح»، ولا يلزم من حين من الأربع أو الخمس مميزاً، ولا أن يكون كل الصبيان في هذا السن مميزين، وقيل: الأقل خمسة عشر، وهو منقول عن ابن معين قال الإمام أحمد هذا عجيب منه والحق أن التقديرات المذكورة لا تستحق أن يلتفت إليها والأصح عدم التقدير بسن) فإن العقل يقوى قليلاً قليلاً من الرحمة الإلهية لا يقدر الإنسان على تقدير قدر منه، ويختلف هذا القدر
Introduction: On the conditions of riwaya (among them is intellect and discernment (for tahammul) i.e., for receiving hadith. And they differed in determining the least number of years by which discernment is acquired. It is said: five, which is the chosen opinion of Ibn al-Salah, as Mahmud ibn al-Rabi' said: 'I understood the spittle that the Messenger of Allah, his family and companions spat, and I was five years old.' Bukhari narrated it. And it is said: four, due to the hadith of the spittle, and this proponent claimed that the correct view is that Mahmud ibn al-Rabi' was four, not five, in the authentic version. And it does not necessarily follow that at the time of four or five one is discerning, nor that all boys at this age are discerning. And it is said: the least is fifteen, which is narrated from Ibn Ma'in. Imam Ahmad said: this is strange from him. And the truth is that the mentioned estimations do not deserve attention. And the most correct is no estimation by age. For the intellect strengthens little by little from divine mercy; a human cannot estimate a portion of it, and this portion differs.
Source pages p. 170

Commentary
This passage is an usul text on the conditions for the transmission of hadith. It discusses the first condition: intellect ('aql) and discernment (tamyiz) for tahammul (receiving hadith). The author presents differing opinions on the minimum age at which tamyiz is achieved. Some say five years, based on the hadith of Mahmud ibn al-Rabi', who reported an incident from his childhood at age five. Others say four, interpreting the same hadith differently. A third opinion sets the minimum at fifteen, attributed to Ibn Ma'in, which Imam Ahmad finds strange. The author of the commentary argues that all these age estimates are unreliable, and the correct view is that there is no fixed age. Intelligence grows gradually by divine mercy, and it varies from person to person. Therefore, tamyiz is determined on a case-by-case basis, not by a specific age.

Key Terms
التمييز (tamyiz): The ability to discern and understand spoken words, distinguishing this from pure memorization without comprehension.
التحمل (tahammul): The act of receiving and comprehending a hadith from a teacher for the purpose of transmission.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ‘most correct’ view according to the text regarding the age of tamyiz for hadith transmission?
A) Five years.
B) Four years.
C) Fifteen years.
D) No fixed age; it varies by individual.

Key Takeaway
Tamyiz is a condition for hadith transmission, but its attainment is not bound by a specific age; it depends on the individual's intellectual development.

Accepting Reports from the Fasiq: Hanafi Exceptions for Hardship and Special Roles
Continuation of discussion on accepting news from fasiq in practical matters

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the conditions for accepting a report from a fasiq in different scenarios (gift, agency, third-party, dar al-harb) and apply the Hanafi principles of istihsan and qiyas khafi to determine when 'adalah is required.

Core Idea
Necessity (haraj) can relax the requirement of 'adalah for accepting khabar, but the scope depends on the reporter's role and the nature of the obligation.

This lesson examines the Hanafi school's nuanced approach to accepting reports from sinful (fasiq) individuals. While 'adalah is a standard condition for testimony, it is not always required for reports in practical matters. The passage from Fawatih al-Rahmut illustrates how the schools within Hanafism weigh hardship (haraj) against the need for verification, leading to different rulings for gifts, agency, third-party reports, and religious obligations in dar al-harb. Understanding these distinctions is key to applying the usul principles of istihsan and qiyas.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenarios
The passage discusses four contexts: (1) gift acceptance, (2) report from an agent/messenger, (3) report from a third-party (mukhbit fuduli), and (4) report in dar al-harb regarding religious obligations. List them and note the ruling for each.
The first two are more lenient; the third has an intra-Hanafi dispute; the fourth has multiple views based on hardship.
2
Analyze the basis for each exception
For gifts, hardship (haraj) is cited—rarely finding an 'adil person. For the agent, the agent stands in place of the principal, so their word is his word. For the third-party, qiyas khafi: the reporter partakes of both testimony (shahada) and mere news, so both rulings are combined. For dar al-harb, extreme hardship due to scarcity of 'adil reporters.
Note that the agent's report is accepted even if fasiq because the agent is essentially the principal's voice.
3
Examine the intra-Hanafi dispute on third-party reports
Imam Abu Hanifa requires either two witnesses or a single 'adil reporter. Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) require only tamyiz (discernment) and truthfulness in the heart. The text declares al-azhar (the most apparent) is Sahibayn's view, because necessity is already met by the exceptions for agents and messengers.
This is a classic example of usul disagreement based on weighing haraj against the need for verification.
4
Apply the principle to dar al-harb
Three views are mentioned: (1) require 'adalah because it is a religious matter, (2) follow the same disagreement as in third-party, (3) Shams al-A'immah's view: no 'adalah required at all due to extreme hardship. The text implies preference for the third view, as it prevents neglect of obligations.
This demonstrates that istihsan (juristic preference) based on haraj can override normal conditions.
5
Evaluate the qiyas khafi and the refutation
The argument that the reporter in dar al-harb is a 'messenger of the Messenger' is refuted by analogy to hadith narration (riwaya), where uprightness is required. The distinction is that this is a specific man delivering a specific report, not a general narration. The final justification is haraj, not mere analogy.
This refines the scope of the rule: the leniency is limited by the context of hardship.

With him that my master sent myself to you as a gift, her word is accepted and intercourse with her is permissible, to repel hardship. For if uprightness were stipulated, the affair of livelihood would be disordered, for rarely does a person find an upright person to deal with or to send witnesses with gifts. How so, and the Prophet (peace and blessings be upon him and his family) used to accept news about gifts from the righteous and the sinful, the free and the slave. And indeed the Prophet (peace and blessings be upon him) accepted the gift of Salman when he was a Christian slave. And [there is] what involves an obligation from one aspect but not another, like the dismissal of an agent and the restriction of a permitted slave and similar matters, for this news strips the reporter of established authority and nothing of the claim is incumbent upon him. So the agent and the messenger from the dismisser and the restrictor, as before, their word is accepted even if they are sinful or a slave, because they stand in the place of the principal and the sender, so their word is his word. And the Imam stipulated for the third-party reporter one of the two halves of testimony: number or uprightness, because when it partakes of two similarities, he acted upon both, giving the ruling of each from one aspect. So if the agent acted after a report from a single sinful person, his action is valid – contrary to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). For they say that it is like the first case; nothing is stipulated except discernment and affirmation of the heart due to necessity. We say: necessity has been removed by the lack of stipulation in the messenger and the agent. So ponder, and the more apparent is their view. And concerning the obligation of religious duties upon one who accepts Islam in dar al-harb through the report of a single sinful or disbelieving person, there is disagreement. It is said: uprightness is required because it is a religious matter. And it is said: it is upon the disagreement between the Imam and his two companions as in the third category. And it is said: the correct view is that there is no condition of uprightness of the reporter at all, so that acts of worship become obligatory upon him, and he must make up if he does not perform them, based on the report of a sinful person. This is stated by Shams al-A'immah. Because the reporter is the messenger of the Messenger, and nothing is stipulated in the report of a messenger. And this is refuted by narration, for the narrator of hadith is also a messenger of the Messenger. And the truth is that the lack of stipulation is specifically for a specific man delivering a specific report; thus uprightness was not required in transactions, and it does not necessitate absolute absence. And the truth in the inference is that stipulation was not considered here because of great hardship. For a righteous person rarely manages to arrive here. So if the word of the sinful and the disbeliever were not accepted and he were permitted to omit the acts of worship, that Muslim would not attain human perfection and would become like animals. So understand.
Source pages p. 170

Commentary
This passage from the sharh of Musallam al-Thubut discusses the acceptance of reports (khabar) from sinful (fasiq) or disbelieving individuals in practical matters (mu'amalat) and religious obligations in dar al-harb. The author begins by giving an example of accepting a gift of a slave girl based on the report of the sender, even if the sender is a sinner, because requiring uprightness would cause hardship in daily life. He further cites the Prophet's acceptance of gifts from both righteous and sinful people, and specifically from Salman when he was a Christian slave. The discussion then moves to reports that involve removing authority, such as an agent dismissing himself or a master restricting a permitted slave (ma'dhun). In these cases, the agent's word is accepted even if he is sinful, because he stands in the place of the principal. Next, a distinction is made for a third-party reporter (mukhbit fuduli). Here, Imam Abu Hanifa stipulates either number (two witnesses) or uprightness if alone, because this report partakes of both testimony (shahada) and mere news. However, his two disciples (Sahibayn) hold that only tamyiz (discernment) and truthfulness in the heart are needed due to necessity. The author remarks that the more apparent view (al-azhar) is that of the Sahibayn, as necessity is already addressed by the exception for agents and messengers. Finally, the passage addresses the obligation of religious duties (shara'i') on a person who accepts Islam in dar al-harb based on the report of a single fasiq or kafir. Three views are mentioned: (1) requiring uprightness because it is a religious matter, (2) following the same disagreement as between Imam and Sahibayn, and (3) the view of Shams al-A'immah that no uprightness is required at all, so that the person becomes obligated to perform acts of worship and must make up missed ones. The reasoning is that this reporter is a messenger of the Messenger (i.e., conveying the message of Islam), and a messenger's report is accepted without conditions. A counterargument from riwaya (hadith narration) is refuted by specifying that this applies to a specific messenger delivering a specific report. The ultimate justification is hardship: requiring uprightness would rarely be possible, so accepting the report of a fasiq or kafir is necessary to avoid preventing the Muslim from achieving human perfection through worship. The author concludes by emphasizing this point.

Key Terms
عدالة ('adalah): Uprightness; a condition for accepting testimony and reports in some contexts
فاسق (fasiq): A sinner; one whose uprightness is not established
مخبر فضولي (mukhbit fuduli): A third-party reporter who is not an agent or messenger; intervenes to convey news
حرج (haraj): Hardship or difficulty; a basis for relaxing rules in Islamic law

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, which view is considered الأظهر (most apparent) regarding the condition for accepting the report of a فضولي (third-party reporter)?
A) The report requires either two witnesses or one 'adil reporter (Imam Abu Hanifa).
B) The report requires only tamyiz and truthfulness, no 'adalah (Sahibayn).
C) The report requires both number and 'adalah.
D) The report requires at least four witnesses.

Key Takeaway
The acceptance of reports from a fasiq in Hanafi usul is not absolute; it depends on the role of the reporter and the degree of hardship, with istihsan often relaxing the condition of 'adalah.

Condition of Tamyiz for Hadith Reception
Introduction to condition of tamyiz for tahammul, with dispute over age and Hanafi resolution

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Hanafi condition for tamyiz in hadith reception and state why no fixed age is required.

Core Idea
Tamyiz is determined by understanding and response, not by a fixed age.

This lesson introduces the first condition for receiving hadith: tamyiz (discernment). The passage discusses the scholarly disagreement on the minimum age for tamyiz and presents the Hanafi view that it is based on the individual's capacity rather than a numerical age.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition
The passage states that the first condition for tahammul is 'aql (intellect) and tamyiz (discernment). Define tamyiz as the ability to understand speech and respond appropriately.
2
Note the disagreement
Various ages are proposed: 5, 4, 15. The passage cites the hadith of Mahmud ibn al-Rabi' and other estimates.
3
Understand the Hanafi position
The author rejects fixed ages, arguing that intellect develops gradually and varies. The correct criterion is understanding and responding.
4
Recognize exceptional cases
Early understanding (e.g., Mahmud at 4-5, al-Shafi'i at 5, al-Tustari at 2) are miracles not generalizable.
5
Conclude with the general rule
If a child demonstrates understanding, his reception is accepted. Generally, this occurs around age 7.

(و) الشرط (للأداء الكمال للعقل، وهو أيضاً مختلف باختلاف الرجال، فلا يمكن تعيين قدر منه فأدير سببه مقامه شرعاً، كما في السفر والمشقة، قال (ومعياره البلوغ سالماً) عن العته والجنون وإنما شرطنا نفس التمييز للتحمل وكماله للأداء (قياساً على الشهادة) لكونهما إخبارين (و لقبولهم) عبد الله بن عباس و) عبد الله بن الزبير والنعمان بن بشير (وأنس بن مالك رواياتهم بلا استفسار منهم أنهم تحملوا قبل البلوغ أو بعده، فعلم أن البلوغ ليس شرطاً عند التحمل وأما اشتراطه عند الأداء فيجيء وجهه.

رضي
،
Introduction: On the conditions of narration. Among them is intellect and discernment for receiving, i.e., for receiving hadith. And they differed in determining the minimum years by which discernment is acquired. It was said: five – and this is the chosen view of Ibn al-Salah, as Mahmud ibn al-Rabi' said: I understood a spit that the Messenger of God (peace and blessings be upon him and his family and companions) spat, and I was five years old – narrated by al-Bukhari. And it was said: four, due to the hadith of the spit, and this claimant alleged that the correct view is that Mahmud ibn al-Rabi' was four in the sahih. And it does not follow that at the age of four or five one is discerning, nor that all children at this age are discerning. And it was said: the minimum is fifteen, and this is transmitted from Ibn Ma'in. Imam Ahmad said: this is amazing from him. And the truth is that the mentioned estimates do not deserve attention, and the most correct is not to estimate by age, for the intellect strengthens little by little from divine mercy, and man cannot estimate a specific amount of it, and this amount varies among children. Rather, the estimate is by understanding speech and responding. So when the child is such that he understands speech and responds, he is fit to receive hadith. But generally, he is not in this state before reaching seven, so guardians are ordered to command them to pray when they reach this age. As for Mahmud al-Rabi' understanding at five or four, and Imam al-Shafi'i memorizing al-Muwatta' when he was five, and Imam Sahl ibn 'Abd Allah al-Tustari memorizing some litanies when he was two, these are among the miracles; the general rule is not built upon them. Yes, if one is found with these attributes, his reception is absolutely accepted, and therefore we did not stipulate a specific age, but it is rarely found. So understand. And the condition for performance is perfection of intellect, and this also varies among men, so a specific amount cannot be assigned. So its cause has been made to stand in its place legally, as with travel and hardship. He said: and its standard is puberty, free from insanity and madness. And we only stipulated discernment itself for reception and its perfection for performance, by analogy with testimony, because both are reports. And because they accepted the narrations of 'Abd Allah ibn 'Abbas, 'Abd Allah ibn al-Zubayr, al-Nu'man ibn Bashir, and Anas ibn Malik without asking them whether they received before puberty or after. So it is known that puberty is not a condition for reception, while its stipulation for performance will have its justification later. And know that 'Abd Allah ibn 'Abbas was born three years before the Hijrah according to al-Waqidi, so his age at the Prophet's death was thirteen years. Also in al-Isti'ab. And Ibn 'Abd al-Barr said about him: We have narrated from multiple chains from Sa'id ibn Jubayr from Ibn 'Abbas: The Messenger of God (peace be upon him) died and I was ten years old, and I had read al-Muhkam, meaning al-Mufassal. Then it was narrated by another chain from the path of 'Abd Allah from his father with his chain from Ibn 'Abbas: The Messenger of God (peace be upon him) died and I was fifteen years old. And al-Bukhari narrated that he was approaching puberty during the days of the Farewell Pilgrimage. So then, his puberty at the time of reception is not confirmed at all. Likewise 'Abd Allah ibn al-Zubayr, the first child born in Islam, after the Hijrah by one or two years according to the well-known view, and it was said in the first year. So all his listening was before puberty, for the Prophet's stay in Medina was ten years. Likewise al-Nu'man ibn Bashir, the first child born among the Ansar after the Hijrah, and the Prophet died while he was eight years old, and it was said six. Ibn 'Abd al-Barr said in al-Isti'ab: the first is more correct, God willing, because most say that he and Ibn al-Zubayr were born two years after the Hijrah. And al-Tabari narrated that Ibn al-Zubayr said: al-Nu'man ibn Bashir and 'Abd Allah... older than me by six months. So all his listening was also before puberty. As for Anas ibn Malik, he was ten years old when the Prophet came to Medina and twenty when he died, so most of his listening was before puberty, and they accepted all of it. As for what Ibn 'Abd al-Barr narrated that he witnessed Badr, his witnessing was not for fighting but for serving the Prophet (peace be upon him), for he was his servant, may God be pleased with him. So it has become clear to you that the best way of inference is to say: because their narrations (peace be upon them) were before puberty – so understand. And it was argued that the practice of the Salaf was to make children listen, so if their narrations were not accepted, there would be no benefit in that. And the author did not approve. And he said: As for making children listen, it is not necessitating of the desired conclusion, due to the possibility of seeking blessing and accustoming to narration, and these are among the greatest benefits. And it was said: the adolescent is accepted.
Source pages p. 170

Commentary
This passage from the sharh introduces the conditions for narrating hadith (شرائط الرواية). The first condition is discrimination (tamyiz) for reception (tahammul). The author summarizes the scholarly disagreement on the minimum age for tamyiz: some say 5 years (Ibn al-Salah, based on the hadith of Mahmud ibn al-Rabi'), others 4 years, others 15 years (attributed to Ibn Ma'in). The correct view, however, is that no specific age is fixed; rather, the criterion is the child's actual ability to understand speech and respond appropriately. This generally occurs around age 7, which is why children are commanded to pray at that age. Exceptional cases of early understanding (e.g., Mahmud at 4/5, al-Shafi'i at 5, al-Tustari at 2) are miracles and not the basis for the general rule. For performance (ada'), complete intellect is required, and its legal standard is puberty (bulugh) free from insanity, analogous to testimony. The passage then provides evidence from the Sahaba: Ibn 'Abbas, Ibn al-Zubayr, al-Nu'man ibn Bashir, and Anas ibn Malik all narrated hadith that they had received before puberty, and the Muslim community accepted their narrations. This proves that puberty is not a condition for tahammul. Detailed biographical notes on Ibn 'Abbas and others are given to show that their pre-pubescent listening is well-attested. The final part discusses an objection: if the Salaf made children listen, it might be for baraka or practice, not necessarily for acceptance of their narrations. The author responds that although that is possible, the fact that they accepted their narrations without inquiry shows that the intention was acceptance. The text concludes with a note that some consider the adolescent (murahiq) acceptable as well.

Key Terms
التمييز (al-tamyiz): The ability to understand speech and respond appropriately, required for tahammul of hadith
التحمل (al-tahammul): The act of receiving and memorizing hadith
الأداء (al-ada'): The act of transmitting hadith

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the correct condition for a child's ability to receive hadith (tahammul)?
A) Reaching the age of five years.
B) Reaching the age of seven years.
C) Being able to understand speech and respond appropriately.
D) Being at least ten years old.

Key Takeaway
Tamyiz in Hanafi usul is a matter of individual capacity, not a fixed age.

Condition of Complete Intellect for Hadith Performance and Evidence from the Sahaba
Explanation of condition for performance and evidence from Sahaba

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the condition of complete intellect (bulugh) for hadith performance and cite the evidence from the Sahaba that puberty is not required for reception.

Core Idea
Puberty is required for performance but not for reception; the Sahaba narrated before puberty.

This lesson covers the second condition: complete intellect for ada' (performance). The passage uses qiyas on testimony and provides evidence from four Sahaba who narrated hadith they heard before puberty.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition for ada'
The passage states that for performance (ada'), complete intellect is required, and its legal standard is puberty free from insanity. Contrast with tahammul which only requires tamyiz.
2
Understand the qiyas on shahadah
The condition is derived by analogy with testimony (shahadah), since both are reports. For testimony, puberty is required, so for hadith narration, it is also required.
3
List the Sahaba evidence
The narrations of four Sahaba (Ibn Abbas, Ibn al-Zubayr, al-Nu'man ibn Bashir, Anas) were accepted even though they heard and narrated before puberty. This proves that puberty is not a condition for tahammul.
4
Analyze the biographical details
Details about each Sahabi's age at the Prophet's death are given to confirm their pre-pubescent listening. For example, Ibn Abbas was 10-15, Ibn al-Zubayr was young, etc.
5
Conclude with the principle
Reception is valid if the child has tamyiz; performance requires puberty. The Salaf's practice of making children listen supports this, though some argue it was for blessing, but acceptance of their narrations shows it was for acceptance.

(فمنها التعقل) والتمييز (للتحمل) أي لتحمل الحديث، وقد اختلفوا في تعيين أقل السنين التي يحصل بها التمييز فقيل : خمسة، وهو المختار عند ابن الصلاح، كما قال محمود بن الربيع : عقلت مجة مجها رسول الله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم وأنا ابن خمس سنين رواه البخاري وقيل أربعة لحديث المجة وزعم هذا القائل بأن الصحيح أن محمود بن الربيع كان هذا الحديث أنه لا يكون الأقل المجة ابن أربع في الصحيح»، ولا يلزم من حين من الأربع أو الخمس مميزاً، ولا أن يكون كل الصبيان في هذا السن مميزين، وقيل: الأقل خمسة عشر، وهو منقول عن ابن معين قال الإمام أحمد هذا عجيب منه والحق أن التقديرات المذكورة لا تستحق أن يلتفت إليها والأصح عدم التقدير بسن) فإن العقل يقوى قليلاً قليلاً من الرحمة الإلهية لا يقدر الإنسان على تقدير قدر منه، ويختلف هذا القدر باختلاف الصبيان (بل) التقدير (بفهم الخطاب ورد الجواب فإذا كان الصبي بحيث يفهم الخطاب، ويرد الجواب يكون صالحاً لتحمل الحديث، لكن في الغالب لا يكون على هذه الحيثية قبل بلوغ السبعة ولذا أمر الأولياء بأمرهم بالصلاة حين بلوغهم هذا السن، وأما تعقل محمود بن الربيع سنة خمس أو أربع وحفظ الإمام الشافعي الموطأ» وهو ابن خمس وحفظ الإمام سهل بن عبد الله التستري بعض الأوراد وهو ابن سنتين، فمن جملة الكرامات لا يبنى عليه الأمر في الغالب. نعم : لو وجد على هذه الصفات تحمله البتة، ولذا ما شرطنا صح سناً، لكنه قلما يوجد فافهم .
